#
<a name="_toc218024785"></a>**HOW TO SHADOWRUN** \

=================================================

Diving into a new RPG system can be daunting, so here’s a recommended approach to getting to know this edition of Shadowrun in a manageable way: 
### **STEP 1 – Get to know the universe (a little)** 
Obtain a rough idea of the Shadowrun universe, i.e. the setting of this RPG. The lore of this universe is *very, very* detailed – don’t feel like you need to know everything. Knowing “a little about a lot” will go a long way here. Here are some starter concepts to learn *a little* about: 

- - History in the Shadowrun universe was the same as IRL up to what year? 
- - What is Goblinification? 
- - What role does magic play in this universe? 
- - What is The Matrix? 
- - What are Megacorporations?  
- - What are Shadowrunners and what role do they play? 

**Recommended resources for your research:** 

- - [“Shadowrun Lore” YouTube playlist](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ctJx6lCH0Rg&list=PLl1ffEF0w9j0-zsDASBLtF_E7nEeJUeRt)
- - [“Edge of Now” PDF](https://1drv.ms/b/c/a73fd13bc13e0f03/IQDCsBG4gE_CR7bcaJ9YHKCCAXTHSTin8wGzGBoOU3JD9QI?e=MuyZF7) 
### **STEP 2 – Get to know the game play mechanics (a little)** 
Read through the “BASIC GAMEPLAY MECHANICS” section of this rulebook. This will help you understand the actual in-game impact of the various decisions to be made during character creation. 
### **STEP 3 – Get to know the various character elements (a little)**  
It’s important not to *commit* to any character ideas yet. First, gain a basic understanding of Shadowrun character creation by skimming through a few key sections of this rulebook, listed below. As you skim, you might like to consider the broad type/s of character/s you might enjoy playing, but don’t set anything in stone. 

- - Metatypes 
- - Attributes
- - Skills
- - Magic & Technomancy Traits 
- - Decking/Rigging (see “The Matrix” section) 
- - Cyberware and Bioware 
### **STEP 4 – Consult the party** 
At this stage, it pays to consult with your fellow players. Discuss the characters you’re each interested in playing and see if you can agree upon a variety of different roles/skills, avoiding too much overlap and covering a range of abilities. 

**Consider party roles/skills like:** 

- - The “face” 
- - Stealth
- - Ranged damage 
- - Melee damage 
- - Non-lethal takedowns
- - Breaking and entering
- - Disabling security systems 
- - Hacking
- - Healing
- - Countering magical threats
- - Investigation 
- - Driving / piloting 
- - Drone control 
- - Underworld knowledge
### **STEP 5 – Character creation**
Once you’ve got a more solid idea for a character that a.) you’d like to play and b.) will work within your party, you can start creating your character.

**Before** diving into the full “crunch” of the character sheet and worrying about how point buy works etc., consider the following questions in this order first. Copy/paste this table to take rough notes as you go.  

|**1**|Do you want your character to be **magical, a technomancer, or neither?**||
| :-: | :- | :- |
|**2**|Which **Skills** do you want your character to have?|<p>Definitely want these: </p><p></p><p>Would like these: </p><p></p><p>These would be a cool/fun bonus: </p><p></p>|
|**3**|Which **Attributes** will best support these skills?|<p>Definitely: </p><p></p><p>Some points in these would also be good:</p><p></p>|
|**4**|Are there any particular **Metatype/s (or Metavariant/s)** that have strengths or bonuses in those Attribute/s?||

Now you’re ready (well, as you’ll ever be!) to dive into the crunch. Open up your character sheet and complete it by starting with the “Character Creation” section of this rulebook and working your way forward from there. Breaking this up into more than one session is a good idea. Once you reach the end of “Equipment”, including “Vehicles”, you’re done! 
### **STEP 6 – Check you’ve covered everything**   
Use the checklist below to ensure your character isn’t missing any crucial elements: 

☐ Metatype selected

☐ Magic, Resonance or Mundane chosen

☐ Attributes include modifications for bioware/cyberware

☐ Skills selected

☐ Knowledges and Languages selected

☐ Qualities selected

☐ Contacts selected

☐ Lifestyle selected

☐ Equipment selected

☐ Nuyen remaining is under 5,000

☐ PAN created


☐ Do you have a Commlink, Cyberdeck or RCC?

☐ Do you have a way to carry or store your gear?

☐ Do you have a SIN?

☐ Do you way of travelling from A to B (car, motorcycle, bus pass)?

☐ Can you deal damage in melee and at range?

☐ Can you be stealthy enough to avoid waking a sleeping guard?

☐ Do you have a silent or quiet way of dealing damage?

☐ Can you move about the city without people calling the police after looking at you?


**BASIC GAMEPLAY MECHANICS**\

============================
### **Hits & Thresholds**
- *Shadowrun* uses **6-sided dice.**
- The number of dice rolled for any test is determined by the character’s relevant skill – the better they are at what they’re attempting to do, the more dice the player will roll.
- For each die rolled, a result of a **5 or 6 is a “hit”**.
- All tests are rolled against a **threshold** – the number of hits required to succeed, which is proportional to the difficulty of the test. The number of hits must either meet or beat the threshold** to succeed. An easy test may require 1 hit (i.e. a threshold of 1), the average is 2 and a hard test may require 4.
- Any number of hits rolled in excess of the threshold is referred to as your **net hits**. These can have positive effects such as increasing the damage you do in combat or the speed with which a task is accomplished.
### **Glitches**
- If more than half the dice rolled show a 1, this is a **glitch** – something bad happens. 
- It is possible to roll a glitch on a test that has enough hits to be successful. The glitch does **not** cancel the success; instead, the glitch occurs in addition to the success.
- If you roll a glitch and also do not achieve a single hit, this is a **critical glitch** – something extremely bad happens.
- *Note*: The *Close Call* use of Edge (see below) can be used to negate a glitch or reduce a critical glitch to a glitch.
### **Limits**
- A **limit** indicates the maximum hits from your initial roll that can be applied to the test. 
- Limits are determined by your attributes (see below) or your equipment (see below).
- *Note*: The *Push the Limit* use of Edge (see below) can be used to remove the limit from a test.
### **Teamwork Tests**
- Choose a leader for the teamwork test. All others serve as assistants.
- Each assistant rolls the appropriate skill + attribute. For each assistant that scores at least one hit, the limit for the leader’s test increases by one.
- Additionally, each hit the assistants make adds one die to the leader’s dice pool.
- The most dice that can be added to the test is equal to the leader’s rating in the applicable skill or the highest attribute rating if the test involves two attributes.
- If any assistant rolls a critical glitch, then the leader receives no bonus to their relevant limit or additional dice from any of the assistants.
- The leader then rolls their adjusted dice pool and tries to beat the threshold for the test.



**<a name="_toc218024787"></a>CHARACTER CREATION**\

==================================================
### **Point Buy**
The Point Buy method has greater flexibility than any other system; the trade-off, of course, is that the complete range of options available can make character creation a somewhat time-consuming process. For many though, the time investment is worth it, as you have the chance to design a character precisely the way you want it to be.

- In the Point Buy system, you **start with 800 Karma** to spend.
- First, select a Metatype, followed by Magic or Resonance type if desired. 
- Then spend Karma to buy attributes, skills, qualities and nuyen. 
- Nuyen is then spent on lifestyle and gear with a maximum of 5,000¥ remaining at the start of the game.
- Language and knowledge skills, and contacts, are purchased with their own points systems, determined by relevant attributes.


**<a name="_toc218024788"></a>METATYPES**\

=========================================
### **Human** 
**Human *(Homo sapiens sapiens)*** is the metatype that has been around the longest. You know them, you love them and if you’re reading this there’s a high probability that you are one. They are balanced in their abilities and tend to have a little larger portion of luck (represented by Edge) than other metatypes. **(Cost = 0 Karma)**
### **Dwarf**
**Dwarfs *(Homo sapiens pumilionis)***, as you may guess, are shorter and stockier than humans. They tend to be quite strong and very resilient, able to recover from damage ranging from knocks to the head to doses of hemlock. Or knocks to the head with a club wrapped in hemlock leaves. Dwarves are hard workers and tend to be highly valued by corporations, which means they are more deeply integrated into human society than the other metatypes. They still face discrimination due to their size and they often have to take steps to make a world built for humans suitable for them. **(Cost = 50 Karma)**
#### **Metavariant subspecies: Gnome**
The gnome variant of the ***Homo sapiens pumilionis***, subspecies maintains the standard thermographic vision, slightly pointed aural helix and extended lifespan of the primary subspecies. Where the subspecies varies physically is in body hair, lessened height and musculature. The gnome metavariant lacks the distinctive body hair of their primary species; in fact, they lack all body hair except for head hair which is usually dark brown or black. Though standard dwarves are short of stature, gnomes are smaller still, with heights rarely exceeding 1.0 metre, averaging only 85 centimetres. Body masses average under 30 kilograms due to the metatype’s dense musculature. This dense muscle on a smaller frame allows gnomes a strength greater than one would expect, though still less than a standard human. **(Cost = 50 Karma)**
### **Elf**
**Elves *(Homo sapiens nobilis)*** are taller than humans, thinner and have pointed ears. They have an extremely annoying knack for being more nimble than humans and they generally are better looking to boot. They also have very long lifespans and continue to look young into their forties and fifties. They have occasionally been known to lord those facts over humans or anyone who comes within hearing range. **(Cost = 40 Karma)**
#### **Metavariant subspecies: Forest Elf**
The forest elf metavariant possesses the same primary physical characteristics of the *nobilis* metatype, with a slight decrease in their average height. The only extensive variation is in their skin. Their epidermal layer integrates sections of cells containing chloroplasts as well as body hair similar to grass. These organelles employ chlorophyll to produce energy through plant-like photosynthesis. **Cost = (50 Karma)**
### **Ork**
**Orks *(Homo sapiens robustus)*** look like the creatures that have been dying by the score in fantasy movies and trideos for almost one hundred and fifty years. With protruding brows, prominent tusks and a large stature, orks have trouble avoiding the stereotype of being unthinkingly violent brutes. It doesn’t help that there are more than a few orks who are happy to live up to that stereotype rather than fight it. The end result is a certain underlying tension between orks and humans, which leads to both groups often preferring to live in separate communities. Elves and orks, on the other hand, often prefer to live in entirely separate countries. Despite the stereotypes, orks can be found in all walks of life, from dank alleys to corporate boardrooms. They have a shorter lifespan than humans, which often leads to them having a certain desperation to pack as much living into their years as they can. **(Cost = 50 Karma)**
#### **Metavariant subspecies: Ogre**
The **Ogre** metavariant possesses the standard low-light vison, muscular bulk, enlarged lower canines and pointed aural helix of their primary subspecies. The variation on standard *homo sapiens robustus* come in smoother skin, a protruding jaw, a wider mouth and a stomach similar to the tin-can-eating goats of urban legend. The ogre metavariant stands at a height similar to standard homo sapiens, though the muscular robustness of the species is still present. Ogres seem even closer to their progenitors due to the smoothness of their skin, a trait often lacking in the standard *robustus*, whose skin is often thick and rough. The jawline and wider mouth of the ogre originally spawned urban legends of cannibalism; these rumours were proven false by the ‘40s, but those raised during the era of its prevalence still feel the effects of this misconception. This urban legend was aided by the fact that ogres can digest almost anything they can swallow. The ability to digest so much leads to obesity and even the most athletic ogres can still have a healthy paunch. **(Cost = 60 Karma)**
### **Troll**
**Trolls *(Homo sapiens ingentis)*** make orks look like the ordinary man on the street. Orks might be, on average, less than a quarter-meter taller than humans; troll, by contrast are more than a half-meter taller than orks. Orks might look like a monstrous version of humanity; trolls, on the other hand, look like vaguely human versions of the creature from your most recent nightmare. With thick, curled horns on their heads (some trolls prefer to have them cut, while others polish them with pride), spiky protrusions of calcium on their joints and individual muscles that are larger than a full-grown pig, trolls give the immediate impression that they are built for destruction. Most of them are able to live up to that image. Not all trolls, though, are about absorbing and inflicting damage. They have tried to find their way into different roles, but their large size combines with cultural stereotypes to make it hard for them to fit it. Orks tend to be the most accepting of trolls and the two metatypes often inhabit the same neighbourhoods. Typically, these are not the most resource-rich neighbourhoods in any given sprawl. **(Cost = 80 Karma)**
#### **Metavariant subspecies: Minotaur**
**Minotaurs** possess the enhanced muscle mass and thermographic vision of the primary *ingentis* subspecies. Variance occurs in their facial and horn structures, height, body hair and dermal deposit formation. Minotaurs get their name from their wide, flattened nasal structure, wide-set eyes and symmetrical horns, which resemble a bull’s face. Minotaur horns are longer than those of trolls, set at a more forward angle and anchored into thick bone plates that allow the horns to withstand greater impact. They are also nearly four times denser than standard *ingentis* horns. These features allow minotaurs to use their horns in more aggressive ways. Minotaurs also average 10 centimetres shorter than trolls but tend to carry the same bulk with added width, further lending to their bullish appearance. This *ingentis* metavariant usually possesses profuse body hair and a distinct lack of the dermal deposits common to the base subspecies. **(Cost = 90 Karma)**
### **Metatype Attributes**

||**Karma Cost**|**Bonus Racial Attributes**|**Maximum Racial Attributes**|**Racial Bonuses**|
| :- | :- | :- | :- | :- |
|**Human**|0|+1 Edg|Edge 7|None|
|**Dwarf**|50|+2 Bod, +2 Str, +1 Wil|Bod 8, Rea 5, Str 8, Wil 7|Thermographic Vision, +2 dice Pathogen & Toxin Resistance, +20% increased Lifestyle cost|
|**Gnome**|50|+1 Agi, +1 Wil, +1 Log|Bod 4, Agi 7, Str 4, Wil 7, Log 7|+20% increased Lifestyle cost, Arcane Arrester (2), Neoteny, Thermographic Vision|
|**Elf**|40|+1 Agi, +2 Cha|Agi 7, Cha 8|Low-Light Vision|
|**Forest Elf**|50|+1 Agi, +1 Cha|Agi 7, Cha 7|Low-Light Vision, Allergy (Pollutants), Photometabolism|
|**Ork**|50|+3 Bod, +2 Str|Bod 9, Str 8, Log 5, Cha 5|Low-Light Vision|
|**Ogre**|60|+3 Bod, +2 Str, +1 Wil|Bod 9, Rea 5, Str 8, Log 5, Cha 4|Low-Light Vision, Ogre Stomach|
|**Troll**|80|+4 Bod, +4 Str|Bod 10, Agi 5, Str 10, Log 5, Int 5, Cha 4|Thermographic Vision, +1 Dermal Armour, +1 Reach, +100% Lifestyle cost|
|**Minotaur**|90|+5 Bod, +4 Str|Bod 11, Agi 5, Str 10, Log 5, Cha 4|Thermographic Vision, Goring Horns, +1 Reach, +100% Lifestyle cost|
### **Racial Bonuses**
**Arcane Arrester (2)**: When targeted by a spell (including a critter’s Innate Spell), the character is harder to affect. This potent ability makes casting both benevolent and malevolent spells on these characters much more difficult. The character adds 4 dice to their resistance test against any spell. If the spell is one that is not normally resisted (such as invisibility), the character still rolls their Arcane Arrester dice pool and reduces the hits rolled on the Spellcasting Test by any hits they roll. This quality affects spells they cast on themselves.

**Dermal Armour +1**: You gain a +1 Armour bonus (cumulative with other Armour, without adding Encumbrance).

**Goring Horns**: Use Exotic Melee Weapon (Horns) skill. DV (STR+2)P, Reach-, AP -1.

**Low-Light Vision**: You can see normally in light levels as low as starlight. It doesn’t help in total darkness though.

**Neoteny**: Halted physical development that leaves them easily mistaken for children or teenagers. Starting Physical Condition Monitor is reduced by 2.

**Pathogen and Toxin Resistance**: Add a +2 dice pool bonus to resist pathogens and toxins.

**Photometabolism**: Forest elves possess some chloroplast skin and grasslike body hair, that supplements their energy needs via photosynthesis. Even when fully exposed to sunlight, this process only creates enough nourishment to supplement a diet, not to replace it. Reduce their Lifestyle costs by ten percent. However, since the character’s overall physical well-being and energy increase in the sunlight, the character feels uncomfortable at night or in the shade, suffering a -1 dice pool penalty on all Social Tests.

**Reach +1**: You have longer reach, giving you an advantage over enemies with lower reach.

**Thermographic Vision**: You can see into the infrared spectrum, enabling you to see heat patterns. It’s a very practical way to spot living beings in areas of total darkness, to check if a motor or machine has been running lately and so on.
### **Height and Weight**
Choose the height and weight of your character. The table beneath is a guideline to give you an idea of averages for various metatypes. To get a proportional weight, determine the new height as a percentage of the average height, convert that to a decimal number, cube that figure and then multiply it by the average weight.

|**Metatype**|**Sex**|**Av. Height**|**Av. Weight**|**Weight Multiplier**|
| :- | :- | :- | :- | :- |
|**Human**|Female|156 cm|54\.5 kg|1\.00|
||Male|170 cm|70\.0 kg|1\.00|
|**Dwarf**|Female|120 cm|44\.3 kg|1\.8|
||Male|120 cm|44\.3 kg|1\.8|
|**Elf**|Female|175 cm|60\.9 kg|0\.80|
||Male|190 cm|78\.2 kg|0\.80|
|**Ork**|Female|182 cm|110\.0 kg|1\.28|
||Male|190 cm|125\.1 kg|1\.28|
|**Troll**|Female|280 cm|491\.1 kg|1\.57|
||Male|280 cm|491\.1 kg|1\.57|
|**Gnome**|Female|110 cm|22\.8 kg|1\.2|
||Male|110 cm|22\.8 kg|1\.2|
|**Forest Elf**|Female|175 cm|60\.9 kg|0\.80|
||Male|190 cm|78\.2 kg|0\.80|
|**Ogre**|Female|163 cm|104\.9 kg|1\.7|
||Male|170 cm|119\.0 kg|1\.7|
|**Minotaur**|Female|230 cm|277\.4 kg|1\.6|
||Male|230 cm|277\.4 kg|1\.6|


**<a name="_toc218024789"></a>ATTRIBUTES**\

==========================================
### **Minimums and Maximums**
- All characters **start with a score of 1** in all attributes.
- Then add any relevant Bonus Racial Attributes listed in the Metatype Attributes table above. 
- At character creation, the natural **maximum for attribute scores 6** unless otherwise specified in the Metatype Attributes table above. Further, at creation, characters may only have **1 Mental or Physical** attribute at this maximum (this excludes Edge, Magic and Resonance).
### **Physical Attributes**
**Body (BOD)**: Body measures your physical health and resiliency. It affects how much damage you can take and stay on your feet, how well you resist damage coming your way, your ability to recover from poison and diseases and things of that nature.

**Agility (AGI)**: Agility measures things like hand-eye coordination, flexibility, nimbleness and balance. Agility is the most important attribute when it comes to scoring hits during combat, as you need to be coordinated to land your blows, whether you’re swinging a sword or carefully aiming a rifle. It also is critical in non-combat situations, such as sneaking quietly past security guards or smoothly lifting a keycard from its secured position.

**Reaction (REA)**: Reaction is about reflexes, awareness and your ability to respond to events happening around you. Reaction plays an important role in deciding how soon you act in combat and how skilled you are in avoiding attacks from others. It also helps you make that quick turn down a narrow alley on your cycle to avoid the howling gangers on your tail.

**Strength (STR)**: Strength is an indicator of, well, how strong you are. The higher your strength, the more damage you’ll do when you’re raining blows down on an opponent and the more you’ll be able to move or carry when there’s stuff that needs to be moved. Or carried. Strength is also important with athletic tasks such as climbing, running and swimming.
### **Mental Attributes**
**Willpower (WIL)**: Willpower is your character’s desire to push through adversity, to resist the weariness of spellcasting and to stay upright after being nailed in the head with a sap. Whether you’re testing yourself against a toxic wilderness or a pack of leather-clad orks with crowbars, Willpower will help you make it through.

**Logic (LOG)**: The Logic attribute measures the cold, calculating power of your rational mind. Whether you are attempting to repair complicated machinery or patch up an injured teammate, Logic helps you to get things right. Logic is also the attribute hermetic mages use to resist Drain from the spells they rain down on their hapless foes. Deckers also find Logic extremely useful, as it helps them develop the attacks and counterattacks that are part of their online battles.

**Intuition (INT)**: Intuition is the voice of your gut, the instinct that tells you things before your logical brain can figure them out. Intuition helps you anticipate ambushes, notice that something is amiss or out of place and stay on the trail of someone you’re pursuing.

**Charisma (CHA)**: Charisma is your force of personality, the persuasiveness and charm you can call on to get people to do what you want without having to go to the trouble of pulling a gun on them. It’s not entirely about your appearance, but it’s also not entirely *not* about your appearance. What it’s mostly about is how you use what you have – your voice, your face, your words and all the tools at your disposal – to charm and/or intimidate the people you encounter. Additionally, Charisma is an important attribute for shamanic mages, as it helps them resist the damaging Drain from spells they cast.
### **Special Attributes**
**Essence (ESS)**: Essence if your metahumanity encapsulated in a number. In Shadowrun, you have ample opportunities to alter your body or push it beyond its normal limits. Such actions often have a cost and they can result in a loss of a portion of your metahumanity, which means a loss of Essence points. Each character starts with an Essence rating of 6 and it acts as a cap on the amount of alterations you can adopt. When it’s gone, it doesn’t come back. It also affects the Magic and Resonance attributes, as losses in Essence are reflected by losses in Magic and Resonance. Essence loss can also reduce healing rates.

While denizens of the Sixth World are accustomed to seeing a variety of augmentations and alterations to the metahuman form, the “uncanny valley” still exists. The uncanny valley is the disconcerting effect that happens when people see something that is almost, but not quite, metahuman. This is what happens when people see others with augmentations – on some level, people notice there is something less (or more) human about that and they respond to it negatively. The change may not be exactly visible, but it is in some way noticeable – in one way or another, a person has become less human and on some level other people notice this.

**Edge (EDG)**: Edge is the ultimate intangible, that certain something that provides a boost when you need it, that gets you out of a tough spot when the chips are down. It’s not used to calculate dice pools; instead, you spend a point of Edge to acquire a certain effect.

**Magic (MAG)**: If you intend to cast spells or use magic in any way, your character needs to have the Magic attribute. Most individuals do not have this attribute, meaning their rating is zero. The magic attribute measures how capable you are in the arcane arts and how much power you can draw down to help you in your efforts.

**Resonance (RES)**: Resonance is the special attribute for technomancers. Technomancers interface with the Matrix using the power of their mind and Resonance measures the strength of their ability to interact and shape that environment. Non-technomancers have a zero rating for Resonance.
### **Using Edge**
Edge can affect your character’s world in a lot of ways. When you want one of these effects to happen, you must spend a point of Edge. A character can only spend Edge on their own actions; they cannot spend it on behalf of others. No more than 1 point of edge can be spent on any specific test or action at one time. You can spend a point of Edge on every roll during an Extended Test, as long as you have Edge.

**Blitz**: Roll 5D6 (plus your normal modifier) for Initiative for a single Combat Turn.

**Close Call**: Either negate the effects of one glitch or turn a critical glitch into a glitch.

**Dead Man’s Switch**: When you character is about to fall unconscious or die, you can spend a point of Edge to make a Body + Willpower (3) test. If you succeed, you may take a single action before your character blacks out.

**Push the Limit**: Gain a +3 dice pool modifier to your test, either before or after the roll. The Rule of Six applies: for every 6 you roll, count it as a success and then re-roll that die, adding any additional hits from the re-roll to your total. If you decide to use this after rolling, only your Edge dice use the Rule of Six. This use of Edge also allows you to ignore any limit on your test.

**Second Chance**: Re-roll all dice that did not score a hit on a test roll. It cannot be used to negate a glitch or a critical glitch. It does not use the Rule of Six and has no effect on limits.

**Seize the Initiative**: Move to the top of the initiative order, regardless of your Initiative Score for the entire Combat turn.
### **Regaining Edge**
Your character gets one point of Edge back after a fulfilling meal and a good night’s sleep. Additionally, the gamesmaster may reward players with a refreshed point of Edge for situations such as: good roleplaying, heroic acts of self-sacrifice, achievement of important personal goals, succeeding in an important objective, being particularly brave or smart, pushing the storyline forward, impressing the group with humour or drama.
### **Attribute Limits**
- Characters have **three inherent limits** – Physical, Mental and Social – that are derived from their attributes. 
- You only use successes on a roll to the maximum of your limit.
- You can ignore your limit for a single test by spending a point of Edge.

**Physical Limit:** [(Strength x2) + Body + Reaction] /3 (round up)

**Mental Limit:** [(Logic x2) + Intuition + Willpower] /3 (round up)

**Social Limit:** [(Charisma x2)] + Willpower + Essence] /3 (round up)
### **Attribute Karma Cost**
Rating 1 ® 2 (10 Karma)		Rating 2 ® 3 (15 Karma)		Rating 3 ® 4 (20 Karma)

Rating 4 ® 5 (25 Karma)		Rating 5 ® 6 (30 Karma)		Rating 6 ® 7 (35 Karma)

Rating 7 ® 8 (40 Karma)		Rating 8 ® 9 (45 Karma)		Rating 9 ® 10 (50 Karma)

***Note*:** When increasing attributes, ensure racial modifiers are applied **first**, **then** spend points to increase attributes further.
### **Attribute-Only Tests**
While most tests are rolled based on a relevant attribute and skill combined, these tests are based on attributes only:

**Composure (CHA + WIL)**: Some situations are tough to deal with, even for hardened professionals like shadowrunners. When a character is faced with an emotionally overwhelming situation there are only two choices. Stay and fight or turn into a quivering lump of goo. To find out which one happens, make a Willpower + Charisma Test, with a threshold based on the severity of the situation. Take note that repeating similar situations over and again eventually eliminates the need to perform this test. Staring down a group of well-armed gangers will be scary at first, but after a character does it a few times the fear gives way to instinct.

**Judge Intentions (CHA + INT)**: Reading another person is also a matter of instinct. A character can use their instincts to guess at the intentions of another person or to gauge how much they can trust someone. Make an Opposed Intuition + Charisma Test against the target’s Willpower + Charisma. This is not an exact science. A successful test doesn’t mean the target will never betray you (intentions have been known to change) and deceptive characters can gain another’s confidence easily. This primarily serves as a benchmark or gut instinct about how much you can trust the person you are dealing with.

**Lifting/Carrying (BOD + STR)**: 

|**Lift/Carry Type**|**Baseline**|**Strength + Body Test <br>increases max weight by:**|
| :- | :- | :- |
|**Lifting off the ground**|15kg per point of Strength|15kg per hit|
|**Lifting over head, i.e. clean & jerk**|5kg per point of Strength|5 kg per hit|
|**Carrying capacity**|<p>10kg per point of Strength</p><p>*(in gear, without effort)*</p>|10kg per hit|

If a character overburdens themselves with gear, they suffer encumbrance modifiers. For every 15 kilograms (or part thereof) by which you exceed your carrying capacity, you suffer a -1 modifier to your Physical Limit (minimum limit of 1). This means that a character with Strength 3 (Carrying Capacity 30) that is trudging along with 50 kilograms of equipment suffers a -2 penalty to their Physical Limit.

**Memory (LOG + WIL)**: While there are numerous mnemonic devices and even a few select pieces of bioware, designed for remembering information, memory is not a skill. If a character needs to recall information, make a Logic + Willpower Test at the time of memorisation. Each hit adds a die to the Recall Test later on.

Glitches can have a devastating effect on memory. A glitch means the character misremembers some portion of the information, such as order of numbers in a passcode. A critical glitch means the character has completely fooled themselves into believing and thus remembering something that never actually happened.
### **Initiative**
Initiative governs how quickly a character responds in a combat situation.

**Physical Initiative**: (Intuition + Reaction) + 1D6

**Astral Initiative**: (Intuition x2) + 3D6

**Matrix AR Initiative**: (Intuition + Reaction) + 1D6

**Matrix VR Initiative (Cold Sim)**: (Response + Intuition) + 3D6

**Matrix VR Initiative (Hot Sim)**: (Response + Intuition) + 4D6

**Matrix VR Initiative (Technomancer)**: (Resonance + Intuition) + 4D6
### **Condition Monitor Boxes**
Condition Monitors are used to track the damage inflicted on a character. Player characters have two Condition Monitors: one tracks Physical damage, the other tracks Stun damage.

**Physical**: (Body/2) + 8 (round up)

**Stun**: (Willpower/2) + 8 (round up)

**Overflow**: Body
### **Reputation**
When you live on the street, with no identity in the system, your rep is all that you’ve got. To shadowrunners and others who exist between the cracks of society, how they are known (and who knows them) is the only piece of information that stays with them and carries any significance. A good reputation gives a person respect and influence among their peers, allowing them to more easily acquire equipment and favours. Conversely, a bad rep can make dealing with anyone in the shadows more difficult.

**Street Cred**: **Starts at 0.**

Street Cred represents a character’s lifetime accomplishments. The more they’ve done and accomplished, the more respected they’ll be by their peers.

Street Cred is applied as a positive Limit Modifier to all Social Tests in situations where the character’s reputation would be known. It is gained by completing shadowruns.

**Notoriety**: **Starts at 0**, modified by various qualities (Positive: Blandness, First Impression, Lucky; Negative: Addiction, Bad Luck, Combat Paralysis, Elf Poser, Gremlins, Incompetent [any skill], Ork Poser, SINner [criminal SIN only], Spirit Bane, Uncouth, Uneducated)

Notoriety represents the negative side of the character’s reputation. If they are difficult to work with, stubborn, unskilled fatally flawed or prone to failure, word is going to get around about them.

**Public Awareness**: **Starts at 0.**

Public Awareness represents how well the character is known among the media, authorities and public at large. With only a few exceptions, shadowrunners are always working to ensure that the public doesn’t know anything about who they are or what they have done. Corporations and other power groups hire runners when they want something taken care of quietly without a great deal of public attention drawn to it. So, if a runner is doing their job, the public should never know about them. The best shadowrunner is one that Joe Wageslave has never heard of. Only when something goes wrong or the situation is unavoidable do the actions of a runner become public.


**<a name="_toc218024790"></a>MAGIC AND TECHNOMANCY TRAITS**\

============================================================
### **Magic-Users**
#### **Adept: (20 Karma)** 
In the small segment of the world that has Awakened to magic power, there is an even smaller segment who are able to channel the mana into themselves, giving them enhanced physical abilities that make them more than meta-human. They are the physical adepts – or, for those who like fewer words, just adepts – and they are known for their very disciplined self-improvement. They include athletes, martial artists, religious acolyte, exercise gurus and others who seek to combine mind and body. Adepts are concerned with the harmony of body and mind and the strengthening of both and they focus their magical power towards those ends.

In the early days of the Sixth World, when the world saw the rise of people who could use magic to increase their own physical and mental potential, adepts didn’t face the same prejudice as magicians and shamans. Instead, they found themselves facing a mythos generated by corporate trids extolling their magical athleticism. This put adepts up on a pedestal – people either wanted to try to fight them to gain rep or to worship them, thinking that perhaps that would be the path to getting some abilities for themselves.

They have a Magic attribute of 1 and can buy more ranks with Karma.

They gain power points equal to their Magic attribute at character creation. You then spend the Power Points on buying adept powers. The maximum number of levels you can have of any one power is equal to your Magic Rating or up to the limit listed by the power, whichever is less.

Adepts cannot learn skills from the Conjuring, Enchanting or Sorcery skill groups.

Adepts can only astrally perceive if they take the Astral Perception power. Adepts can learn the Assensing skill only if they have the Astral Perception power.

Adepts cannot astrally project.
#### **Aware: (10 Karma)** 
The Aware have **astral perception** as their lone magical ability, a truly minor ability that nonetheless sets them higher than the truly mundane. The aware have been known for ages as readers of auras, palms or other forms of psychometry but simply being able to see magical activity is power enough to serve them as researchers, observing the magic used by others and taking note. The largest place for them, by far, is in the world of security, serving in personal security details to ensure no magic is used to influence negotiations, to keep an eye out for spiritual intrusion or to direct security details against enchanted intruders. Several have found a place as musicians as well, as being able to read the emotional state of a crowd and adjusting their performance to it is a significant asset.

They have a Magic attribute of 1 and can buy more ranks with Karma.

The Aware cannot use skills from the Conjuring, Enchanting or Sorcery skill groups.

The Aware can astrally perceive. The Aware can learn the Assensing skill.

The Aware cannot astrally project.
#### **Conjurer: (20 Karma)**
The character is a magic-user, skilled in Conjuration.

They have a Magic attribute of 1 and can buy more ranks with Karma.

At character creation, Conjurers know summonings equal to their Magic Rating x2.

They may learn the Banishing, Binding and Summoning skills and the Conjuring skill group.

Conjurers cannot use skills from the Enchanting or Sorcery skill groups.

Conjurers can astrally perceive and learn the Assensing skill.

Conjurers cannot astrally project.
#### **Enchanter: (20 Karma)**
` `The character is a magic-user, skilled in Enchanting.

They have a Magic attribute of 1 and can buy more ranks with Karma.

At character creation, Enchanters know a total number of alchemical preparations and foci formula equal to their Magic Rating x2.

They may learn the Alchemy, Artificing and Disenchanting skills and the Enchanting skill group.

Enchanters cannot use skills from the Conjuring or Sorcery skill groups.

Enchanters can astrally perceive and learn the Assensing skill.

Enchanters cannot astrally project.
#### **Sorcerer: (20 Karma)** 
The character is a magic-user, skilled in Sorcery.

They have a Magic attribute of 1 and can buy more ranks with Karma.

At character creation, Sorcerers know a total number of spells and rituals equal to their Magic Rating x2.

They may learn the Counterspelling, Ritual Spellcasting and Spellcasting skills and the Sorcery skill group.

Sorcerers cannot use skills from the Conjuring or Enchanting skill groups.

Sorcerers can astrally perceive and learn the Assensing skill.

Sorcerers cannot astrally project.
#### **Magician: (40 Karma)** 
The character is a magic-user, able to cast spells, conjure spirits and use other magical abilities.

They have a Magic attribute of 1 and can buy more ranks with Karma.

At character creation, Magicians know a total number of summonings, alchemical preparations, spells and rituals equal to their Magic Rating x2.

They may learn the Conjuring, Enchanting and Sorcery skill groups and all the skills therein.

Magicians can astrally perceive and learn the Assensing skill.

Magicians can astrally project.
### **Resonance**
#### **Technomancer: (15 Karma)** 
The character is a technomancer with a Resonance attribute of 1 and can buy more ranks with Karma. 


**<a name="_toc218024791"></a>SKILLS**\

======================================
### **Skill Karma Cost**

|**Rating:**|**1**|**2**|**3**|**4**|**5**|**6**|**7**|
| :- | :- | :- | :- | :- | :- | :- | :- |
|Skill Group|5|15|30|50|75|105|140|
|Skill|2|6|12|20|30|42|56|
|Knowledge Skill\*|1|3|6|10|15|21|28|
|Language Skill\*|1|3|6|10|15|21|28|

*\*Knowledge and Language Skills are first purchased based on their own points system – see “Knowledge and Language Skills” below. The above Karma points can be spent to purchase additional Knowledge Skills and/or Languages, if desired.*
### **What the Ratings Mean**
**Rating 0 - Untrained**: The default level of knowledge. Though untrained, you have a general awareness of the skill and occasionally may even be able to fake it.

**Rating 1 - Beginner**: You have a little training about how it works, but not always why it works.

**Rating 2 - Novice**: You’re a hobbyist, but not an enthusiast.

**Rating 3 - Competent**: You’re skilled at basic operations but struggle with complex operations and “tricks”.

**Rating 4 - Proficient**: You’re comfortable with what you do and perform well under normal pressures. Professional level for most jobs.

**Rating 5 - Skilled**: You know how to handle yourself in unfamiliar situations and can get creative when solving problems.

**Rating 6 - Professional**: You could easily sell your skills on the open market. This is the usual **maximum skill level for starting player characters.**

**Rating 7 - Veteran**: You’ve seen a lot of what the skill can do and what it can’t. Other people ask you how to do it.
### **Skill Groups**
Skill Groups are a collection of skills based around a core concept. You can purchase a skill group for less than it costs to take all the skills in the group individually. Having a skill group at a certain rating is the same as having all the skills in the skill group at that rating.

Skill group advancement uses special rules. If you want to advance one skill from the group without advancing the rest, the skill group is broken and you get each of the skills in the group at the former group rating; then you can increase one of the skills. If you want to get the skill group back (or get a new one), you must first get all the skills in the group to the same rating.

|**Skill Group**|**Skills**|**Non-Group Skills**|||
| :- | :- | :- | :- | :- |
|***Acting***|Con|Impersonation|Performance|Archery|
|***Athletics***|Acrobatics|Running|Swimming|Exotic Ranged Weapons|
|***Biotech***|First Aid|Medicine|Biotechnology|Throwing Weapons|
|***Close Combat***|Blades|Clubs|Unarmed Combat|Perception|
|***Firearms***|Heavy Weapons|Handguns|Longarms|Intimidation|
|***Influence***|Etiquette|Leadership|Negotiation|Artisan|
|***Outdoors***|Survival|Tracking|Animal Handling|Chemistry|
|***Stealth***|Palming|Sneaking|Lockpicking|Demolitions|
|***Vehicular Piloting***|Pilot Aircraft|Pilot Groundcraft|Pilot Watercraft|Gunnery|
|***Cracking***|Hacking|Electronic Warfare|Cybercombat|Pilot Exotic Vehicle|
|***Engineering***|Mechanic|Armourer|Fabrication|Cybertechnology|
|***Electronics***|Software|Computer|Hardware|Arcana|
|***Conjuring***|Banishing|Binding|Summoning|Assensing|
|***Enchanting***|Alchemy|Artificing|Disenchanting|Astral Combat|
|***Sorcery***|Counterspelling|Ritual Spellcasting|Spellcasting||
|***Tasking***|Compiling|Decompiling|Registering||
### **Specialisations**
If you devote extra time to a subset of a skill, it’s called a specialisation. A specialisation adds a +2 dice pool modifier to any test made for that skill when the specialisation comes into play. Characters can have multiple specialisations within the same skill, but only one applies at a time. New characters may only take one specialisation per skill at character creation, but you can buy more later. If you want a specialisation in a skill, you need a rating of at least 1 in that skill. Specialisations are not allowed for skill groups. A specialisation costs 7 karma.
### **Defaulting**
It is impossible to prepare for every scenario and only slightly harder to have every skill. When you perform an action without actually having the skill for the test, there’s still hope. You can **default** the skill, making the test using only the attribute to form the dice pool. You don’t have any tremendous talent when you default – quite the opposite in fact. Defaulting imposes a -1 dice pool modifier in addition to any other modifiers the situation demands. Some skills are too technically demanding to be defaulted. These are mentioned in the skill description.
### **Combat Active Skills**
#### **Archery (Agility):** 
Archery is used to fire string-loaded projectile weapons. An archer is familiar with many different styles of bow and the multitude of arrows that can be used to maximum effect.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Bow, Crossbow, Non-Standard Ammunition
#### **Blades (Agility):** 
Slice and dice! The Blades skill includes the use of all handheld slashing and stabbing weapons. You can use a range of edged weapons including daggers, swords and axes.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Close Combat

Specialisations: Axes, Knives, Swords, Parrying
#### **Clubs (Agility):**
Clubs governs the use of all hand-held bludgeoning instruments. With this skill you can turn any blunt item, be it a baseball bat, crutch or mace, into a weapon.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Close Combat

Specialisations: Batons, Hammers, Saps, Staves, Parrying
#### **Exotic Ranged Weapon [Specific] (Agility):** 
Sometimes a regular gun or blade won’t do the job and you need something fancier. Or weirder. This skill must be taken once for each unusual ranged weapon you want to use. Some examples include blowguns, flamethrowers and bolas.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: None
#### **Handguns (Agility):** 
This skill category includes all types of handheld pistols, including tasers, single-shots, semi-automatics and revolvers as well as machine pistols and submachine guns.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Firearms

Specialisations: Holdouts, Revolvers, Semi-Automatics, Tasers
#### **Heavy Weapons (Agility):** 
The term heavy weapon is designated for all projectile weaponry larger than an assault rifle, such as grenade launchers, machine guns and assault cannons. This skill is exclusive to handheld and non-vehicle-mounted weaponry – if you’ve got a gun mounted on or in a vehicle, use Gunnery.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Firearms

Specialisations: Assault Cannons, Grenade Launchers, Machine Guns, Rocket Launchers
#### **Longarms (Agility):** 
The Longarms skill is for firing extended-barrel weapons such as rifles. This grouping also includes weapons like shotguns that are designed to be braced against the shoulder.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Firearms

Specialisations: Assault Rifles, Shotguns, Sniper Rifles
#### **Throwing Weapons (Agility):** 
Throwing Weapons is a broad-based attack skill that can be used for any handheld item that is thrown by the user as a weapon.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Aerodynamic, Blades, Non-Aerodynamic
#### **Unarmed Combat (Agility):** 
Unarmed Combat covers the various self-defence and attack moves that employ.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Close Combat

Specialisations: Blocking, Subduing or by specific Martial Art
### **Physical Active Skills**
#### **Acrobatics (Agility):** 
Acrobatics measures your balance, general athleticism and all-around ability to use your body. This includes your ability to escape from bindings by using body contortion and manual dexterity as well as skydiving with a parachute, flying a wingsuit or descending on a line, bungee cord or zipline.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Athletics

Specialisations: Balance, Climbing, Handcuffs, Leaping, Parachute, Parkour, Rappelling
#### **Palming (Agility):** 
Palming is sleight-of-hand skill that gives a character the ability to snag, hide and pass off small objects.

Default: No

Skill Group: Stealth

Specialisations: Legerdemain, Pickpocket, Pilfering, Concealment
#### **Perception (Intuition):** 
Perception refers to the ability to spot anomalies in everyday situations, making it one of the key skills a shadowrunner needs.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Hearing, Scent, Taste, Touch, Visual, Numinous
#### **Running (Strength):** 
Running, as you may guess, is about how much ground you can cover quickly.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Athletics

Specialisations: Distance, Sprinting, by Terrain (Desert, Forest, Urban, etc.)

*Note*: Characters are allowed a maximum number of Sprinting tests equal to half their Running Skill per Combat Turn (minimum 1).
#### **Sneaking (Agility):** 
Need to get where you’re not supposed to be? This skill allows you to remain inconspicuous in various situations.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Stealth

Specialisations: Locations type (Desert, Jungle, Urban, etc.)

*Group Stealth Tests: If party members can communicate effectively, then a character with a hit can “give” it to a less skilled character by providing assistance or preventing a misstep. Hits can only be transferred to a maximum of the ranks in Stealth the providing character has.*
#### **Survival (Willpower):** 
Survival is the ability to stay alive in extreme environmental conditions for extended periods of time. This skill governs a character’s ability to perform vital outdoor tasks such as start a fire, build a shelter, scrounge for food, etc. in hostile environments.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Outdoors

Specialisations: By terrain (Desert, Forest, Mountain, etc.)
#### **Swimming (Strength):** 
This skill determines the character’s ability to swim in various bodies of water. The skill level affects the distance and speed at which the character can swim. It also can be used when diving, using complex diving equipment and holding your breath.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Athletics

Specialisations: Dash, Holding Breath, Long Distance, SCUBA
#### **Tracking (Intuition):** 
This skill confers the ability to detect the passage of metahumans and other game through terrain and use those clues to follow that individual. This skill also allows you to identify unmarked trails and common game paths in various environments. It also includes following a course by landmarks or general direction sense.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Outdoors

Specialisations: By terrain (Desert, Forest, Mountain, etc.)
### **Social Skills**

|**NPC’s attitude toward character**|**Dice Modifier**|**General Modifiers**|**Dice Modifier**|**Character’s desired result is:**|**Dice Modifier**|
| :- | :- | :- | :- | :- | :- |
|**Friendly**|+2|Character has (known) street rep|+/- Street Cred|Advantageous to NPC|+1|
|**Neutral**|+0|Character is intoxicated|-1|Of no value to NPC|+0|
|**Suspicious**|-1|Subject has romantic attraction to character|+2|Annoying to NPC|-1|
|**Prejudiced**|-2|Subject has “ace in the hole”|+2|Harmful to NPC|-3|
|**Hostile**|-3|||Disastrous to NPC|-4|
|**Enemy**|-4|||||

#### **Con (Charisma):** 
Con governs the ability to manipulate or fool people during a social encounter. This skill covers a range of confidence games as well as the principles behind those cons.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Acting

Specialisations: Fast Talking, Seduction

*Modifiers:	Subject has time to evaluate the situation -1*

*Subject is distracted +1*

`	`*Character has plausible-seeming evidence +1 or +2*
#### **Etiquette (Charisma):** 
Etiquette represents the level of understanding and awareness of proper social rituals. The skill works as a sort of social version of Sneak, allowing you to move unimpeded through various social situations. Etiquette also serves as a social safety net in case a player botches a social situation in a way a skilled character would not.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Influence

Specialisations: By culture or subculture (Corporate, High Society, Military, Street, Yakuza, etc.)

*Modifiers:	Character is wearing the wrong attire or doesn’t have the right look -1*

*Character is obviously nervous, agitated or frenzied -1*

*Subject is distracted -1 (this applies to the subject’s dice pool)*
#### **Impersonation (Charisma):** 
Impersonation is the ability to assume the identity of another person, including voice and physical mannerisms. This skill is limited by the physical abilities of the character. A dwarf might be able to impersonate a troll over a commlink, but the illusion shatters when he is face to face with his target. It also covers non-magical forms of masking your identity, including makeup and enhancement.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Acting

Specialisations: By metahuman type (Dwarf, Elf, Human, Ork, Troll), Cosmetic, Theatrical
#### **Intimidation (Charisma):** 
Intimidation is about creating the impression that you are more menacing that another person in order to get them to do what you want.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Interrogation, Mental, Physical, Torture

*Modifiers:	Character wielding weapon or obvious magic +2*

*Subject wielding weapon or obvious magic -2*

*Characters outnumber subject(s) +2*

*Subjects outnumber character(s) -2*

*Character is causing (or has caused) subject pain (torture) +2*

*Subject is oblivious to danger or doesn’t think character “would try something so stupid” +2 (this applies to the subject’s dice pool)*
#### **Leadership (Charisma):** 
Leadership is the ability to direct and motivate others. It’s like Con, except rather than using deception you’re using a position of authority. This skill is especially helpful in situations where the will of the teammate is shaken or someone is being asked to do something uncomfortable. The Leadership skill is not meant to replace or make up for poor teamwork.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Influence

Specialisations: Command, Direct, Inspire, Rally

*Modifiers:	Character has superior rank +1 to +3*

`		`*Subject has superior rank -1 to -3*

`		`*Character is an obvious authority figure +1*

`		`*Character not part of subject’s social strata -1 to -3*
#### **Negotiation (Charisma):** 
Negotiation governs a character’s ability to apply their charisma, tactics and knowledge of situational psychology in order to create a better position when making deals.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Influence

Specialisations: Bargaining, Contracts, Diplomacy

*Modifiers:	Character lacks background knowledge of situation -2*

`		`*Character has blackmail material or heavy bargaining chip +2*
#### **Performance [Specific] (Charisma):** 
This skill governs the ability to execute a performing art. Performance is to the arts what Artisan is to craft. The performer uses their skill to entertain or even captivate an audience. This skill must be taken once for each performing art you want to use (e.g. Dance, Singing, Violin, etc.)

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Acting

Specialisations: By performance art (Comedy, Dance, specific Musical Instrument, etc.)
### **Technical Skills**
#### **Animal Handling (Charisma):** 
This skill governs the training, care, riding (if they’re big enough) and control on non-sentient animals. Competent trainers have the ability to handle multiple animals. It is even possible to approach an untrained animal and get it to trust you, or at least not eat you.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Outdoor

Specialisations: By animal (Bird, Dolphin, Horse, etc.), Herding, Riding, Training
#### **Armourer (Logic):** 
Armourer encompasses the broad array of skills required to build and maintain weapons. The proper tools and equipment are required to perform repair and build operations.

Default: No

Skill Group: Engineering

Specialisations: Pistols, Rifles, Weapon Accessories
#### **Artisan [Specific] (Intuition):** 
This skill includes several different forms of artistic expression as well as the handcrafting of fine objects that would otherwise be produced on an assembly line. The world’s top artists and crafters are considered artisans. It also include forging physical documents, seals and IDs. This skill must be taken once for each form of artistic expression you want to use (e.g. Document Forging, Scrimshaw, Woodcrafting).

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: By discipline
#### **Biotechnology (Logic):** 
Biotechnology is a wide-ranging skill primarily used by doctors and scientists to grow organic body parts. This skill is the basic for cloning as well as all forms of bioware. Provided the right equipment is available, biotechnology can be used to repair damaged bioware, clone new tissue or detect any bioware in a subject’s body. This skill does not allow characters to install or remove bioware (see Medicine).

Default: No

Skill Group: Biotech

Specialisations: Bioware, Cloning, Gene Therapy, Vat Maintenance
#### **Computer (Logic):** 
Computer is the base skill for interacting with the Matrix. It represents the ability to use computers and other Matrix-connected devices. The Computer skill focuses on understanding multiple operating systems. I can also be used to create data-based forgeries like electronic documents, emails and SINs. It does not allow the character to exploit code (see Hacking).

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Electronics

Specialisations: Forgeries, Matrix Perception, Matrix Search
#### **Cybercombat (Logic):** 
Cybercombat is the skill used by hackers to engage in combat on the Matrix.

Default: No

Skill Group: Cracking

Specialisations: Devices, IC, Personas, Sprites
#### **Cybertechnology (Logic):** 
Cybertechnology is the ability to create, maintain and repair cybernetic parts. A character with the proper tools and parts may repair or even build new cybernetics. Cybertechnology is not a surgical skill. Characters cannot attach or re-attach cybernetics to organic material with this skill (see Medicine). This skill may be used to modify or upgrade cybernetics within cyberlimbs.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Bodyware, Cyberlimbs, Headware, Repair
#### **Chemistry (Logic):** 
Chemistry permits the character to create chemical reactions and develop chemical compounds ranging from drugs, to perfumes, to biopolymers like NuSkin. Chemistry can also be used to analyse chemical compounds to determine what they are.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Analytical, Biochemistry, Inorganic, Organic, Physical
#### **Demolitions (Logic):**
Demolitions is used to prepare, plant, detonate and often defuse chemical-based explosives.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Commercial Explosives, Defusing, Improvised Explosives
#### **Electronic Warfare (Logic):** 
Electronic Warfare is the basis of signals intelligence. It governs the encoding, disruption, spoofing and decoding and communication systems. Providing the user has the proper equipment, the skill can be used to manipulate or even take over the signal of an item’s communication system.

Default: No

Skill Group: Cracking

Specialisations: Communications, Encryption, Jamming, Sensor Operations
#### **Fabrication (Logic):** 
Fabrication is used to build and repair structures as well as the ability to dismantle them. It includes the ability to weld and wield a jackhammer when required. Fabrication requires the proper tools and time.

Default: No

Skill Group: Engineering

Specialisations: Metalwork, Carpentry, Doors
#### **First Aid (Logic):** 
First Aid is the ability to provide emergency medical assistance similar to that of a paramedic. This skill may be used to stabilise wound and prevent characters from dying. First Aid cannot be used to perform surgery or repair damaged implants.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Biotech

Specialisations: Burns, Fractures, Gunshot Wounds, Open Wounds, Resuscitation
#### **Hacking (Logic):** 
Hacking is used to discover and exploit security flaws in computers and other electronics.

Default: No

Skill Group: Cracking

Specialisations: Devices, Files, Hosts, Personas
#### **Hardware (Logic):** 
Hardware reflects a character’s ability to build and repair electronic devices. A workspace, proper materials and sufficient build time are required to enact a repair or to build a new device.

Default: No

Skill Group: Electronics

Specialisations: Commlinks, Cyberdecks, Smartguns, Security Devices

*Defeating a Transponder-embedded Lock requires a Hardware + Logic [Mental] (Lock Rating, 1 Combat Turn) Extended Test at the same time the lock is picked. If the same character is picking the lock and calibrating the electrical feed, apply a -2 dice pool penalty to both tests.*
#### **Lockpicking (Agility):** 
This skill covers bypassing and opening mechanical and electronic locks. While largely banished to antiquity, traditional mechanical locking mechanisms are still in use around the globe, often as throwbacks or backups. Electronic locks are far more common and quite susceptible to your ministrations.

Default: No

Skill Group: Stealth

Specialisations: Combination, Keypad, Key Lock (Padlock, Deadbolt, etc.), Maglock

*Defeating a Key Lock requires a Lockpicking + Agility [Physical] (Lock Rating, 1 Combat Turn) Extended Test.*
#### **Mechanic (Logic):** 
This skill is concerned with the maintenance and repair of mechanical machines from cars and motorboat engines to large-scale machines such as assembly line equipment. Repairs require the proper tools and time.

Default: No

Skill Group: Engineering

Specialisations: Engine, Hydraulics, Industrial Robotics, Wheeled
#### **Medicine (Logic):** 
Medicine is used to perform advanced medical procedures such as surgeries. It includes long-term medical support for disease and illness and the skill can be used to diagnose a character’s medical condition. This skill is used to implant or remove cybernetics and bioware but cannot be used to repair or maintain implanted devices.

Default: No

Skill Group: Biotech

Specialisations: Diagnosis, Cosmetic Surgery, Extended Care

*If an RFID tag is implanted under the skin, an Extended Medicine + Logic [Mental] (10, 1 minute) Test is needed to remove it.*
#### **Software (Logic):** 
Software is the skill used to create and manipulate programming in the Matrix. It’s also what technomancers use when they create their complex forms.

Default: No

Skill Group: Electronics

Specialisations: DataBombs or by Complex Form (Editor, Resonance Spike, Tattletale, etc.)
### **Vehicle Skills**
#### **Gunnery (Agility):** 
Gunnery is used when firing any vehicle-mounted weapon, regardless of how or where the weapon is mounted. This skill extends to manual and sensor-enhanced gunnery.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Artillery, Ballistic, Guided Missile
#### **Pilot Aircraft (Reaction):**
This skill is used to pilot any manned or unmanned aircraft operating.

Default: No

Skill Group: Vehicular Piloting

Specialisations: Fixed-Wing, Lighter-Than-Air, VTOL
#### **Pilot Exotic Vehicle (Reaction):** 
This skill must be taken once for each unusual vehicle you want to use. For example, submarine, spaceship or hot-air balloon.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: None
#### **Pilot Groundcraft (Reaction):** 
This skill is used to pilot any manned or unmanned aircraft operating.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Vehicular Piloting

Specialisations: Bike, Hovercraft, Tracked, Wheeled
#### **Pilot Watercraft (Reaction):** 
This skill is used to pilot any waterborne vehicle, whether from inside it or by remote control.

Default: Yes

Skill Group: Vehicular Piloting

Specialisations: Hydrofoil, Motorboat, Sailboat
#### **Rig Vehicle (Reaction):** 
This skill can only be used by characters with a Vehicle Control Rig. It is used to pilot vehicles through a vehicle control rig.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Hover, Tracked, Walker, Wheeled
### **Magical Skills**
#### **Alchemy (Magic):** 
Alchemy is used to create substances that store spells. Alchemy is most commonly used to brew potions, distil magical reagents and even create orichalcum.

Default: No

Skill Group: Enchanting

Specialisations: By Spell Type, By Trigger
#### **Arcana (Logic):** 
Arcana governs the creation of magical formulae used to create spells, foci and all other manner of magical manipulations. Arcana is required to understand formulae that may be purchased over the counter or discovered by other means.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Spell Design, Focus Design, Spirit Formula
#### **Artificing (Magic):** 
Artificing is the process of crafting magical foci. The skill may also be used forensically, in order to assense qualities about an existing focus’ creation and purpose.

Default: No

Skill Group: Enchanting

Specialisations: Crafting (by focus type), Focus Analysis
#### **Assensing (Intuition):**
Assensing is a magic user’s ability to read and interpret fluctuations in the astral world. This skill allows practitioners to learn information by reading astral auras. Only characters capable of astral perception may take this skill.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Aura Reading, Astral Signatures, Wards
#### **Astral Combat (Willpower):** 
Fighting in Astral Space requires the Astral Combat skill. Combat in the Astral World relies on a very different set of abilities and attributes than physical combatants.

Default: No

Skill Group: None

Specialisations: Magicians, Mana Barriers, Spirits
#### **Banishing (Magic):** 
This skill is used to disrupt the link between spirits and the physical world. Banished spirits are forced to return to their native plane and are no longer required to complete unfulfilled services.

Default: No

Skill Group: Conjuring

Specialisations: Spirits of Air, Spirits of Earth, Spirits of Fire, Spirits of Man, Spirits of Water
#### **Binding (Magic):** 
This skill is used to compel a summoned spirit to perform a number of additional services.

Default: No

Skill Group: Conjuring

Specialisations: Spirits of Air, Spirits of Earth, Spirits of Fire, Spirits of Man, Spirits of Water
#### **Counterspelling (Magic):** 
Counterspelling is a defensive skill used to defend against magical attacks and dispel sustained magical spells.

Default: No

Skill Group: Sorcery

Specialisations: Combat Spells, Detection Spells, Manipulation Spells
#### **Disenchanting (Magic):** 
This skill governs a character’s ability to remove the enchantment from an item.

Default: No

Skill Group: Enchanting

Specialisations: Alchemical Preparations, Power Foci
#### **Ritual Spellcasting (Magic):** 
This skill is used to cast ritual spells.

Default: No

Skill Group: Sorcery

Specialisations: Anchored, Minion
#### **Spellcasting (Magic):** 
This skill permits the character to channel mana into effects known as spells.

Default: No

Skill Group: Sorcery

Specialisations: Combat Spells, Detection Spells, Manipulation Spells
#### **Summoning (Magic):** 
This skill is used to summon spirits.

Default: No

Skill Group: Conjuring

Specialisations: Spirits of Air, Spirits of Earth, Spirits of Fire, Spirits of Man, Spirits of Water
### **Resonance Skills**
#### **Compiling (Resonance):** 
Compiling involves the ability to translate the complex 0s and 1s of machine source language and the rhythms of the resonance into sprites.

Default: No

Skill Group: Tasking

Specialisations: Data Sprites, Machine Sprites
#### **Decompiling (Resonance):** 
Decompiling is a character’s ability to effectively delete previously complied sprites.

Default: No

Skill Group: Tasking

Specialisations: Courier Sprites, Fault Sprites
#### **Registering (Resonance):** 
This skill allows a technomancer to register sprites on the Matrix, thereby convincing the grids that they are legitimate.

Default: No

Skill Group: Tasking

Specialisations: Crack Sprites, Data Sprites
### **Knowledge and <a name="_hlk209965146"></a>Language Skills**
- - All characters have **one\* language** that they know as their native language. No test is required for a character to communicate in their native language, and as such, the skill is **given for free** and does not have an associated skill rating.** *(**\***Two, if your character has taken the Bilingual quality.)*
- - Other Knowledge and/or Language skills are **purchased with** **bonus points**, separate to Karma,** equal to \
-   **2x (Intuition rating + Logic rating)**, disregarding any boosts from cyberware or bioware.
- - *Once these points have been spent, players can purchase additional Knowledge and/or Language skills, if desired, using Karma, per “Skill Karma Cost” table above.*

**Knowledge and Language skills** otherwise work in the same manner as all other Skills: they have corresponding numerical **ratings** to represent skill proficiency (see “What the Ratings Mean” above) and this rating is combined with an associated Attribute to determine the dice pool for tests.

**Knowledge and Language Skills points cost:** **1 bonus point per skill rating** (see “What the Ratings Mean” above)\
*(E.g. Rating 2 in Astronomy = 2 bonus points)*
### **Language Skills**
- - Language skills use **Intuition** as their linked Attribute.
- - When using Social skills in a foreign language, the language barrier hinders your character’s charms. You can’t add more dice from your Social skill than you have in the language you (attempt to) speak.
#### **Common Shadowrun Languages:** 
English, Spanish, Japanese, Russian, French, Italian, German, Mandarin, Arabic, Dine (Navajo), Lakota, Dakota, Sperethiel (Elven), Or’zet (Orcish)

|**Language Skill Tests**||
| :- | :- |
|Situation|Threshold|
|Universal concept (hunger, fear, bodily function)|1|
|Basic conversation (concerns of daily life)|1|
|Complex subject (special/limited interest topic)|2|
|Intricate subjects (almost any technical subject)|3|
|Obscure subject (very technical/rare knowledge)|4|
|Situation|Dice Pool Modifier|
|Speaking lingo (or variation of particular language)|-2|
|Using AR visual display help|+1 to +4|
### **Knowledge Skills**
There are four types of Knowledge skills:

- - **Academic** knowledge is information gained through formal education, whether from a school, tutor, university or other structured program. 
- - **Interests** include hobbies, experiences and personal interests of the individual character. 
- - **Professional** knowledge comes from an employer or professional organisation. 
- - **Street** knowledge includes everything a runner has picked up from life in the shadows, from drug prices to gang politics who pays the most for stolen goods.

When purchasing knowledge skills, a player should note which of these categories the skill belongs to so they know which **attribute** (see below) they will need to roll on their Knowledge Tests. Sometimes, Knowledge skills may straddle multiple categories. In these cases, choose the most appropriate category for the knowledge skill based on the character and how they would use it. For example, a Corporations Knowledge skill could fit in Professional, Academic or Street categories; a neo-anarchist with this skill would likely be focused on how corporate activities affect life on the street, so for this character it would be a Street skill, while for a boardroom executive it would be Professional.
#### **Common Shadowrun Knowledge Skills:**
**Academic Knowledges (LOG)**: Art, Astronomy, Biology, Economics, Engineering, History, Literature, Mathematics, Ornithology, Parabotany, Parazoology, Philosophy, Physics, Psychology, Religion, Zoology

**Interests Knowledges (INT)**: Anime and Manga, Classic Music, Club Music, Fashion, Gambling, Gardening, Matrix Games, Opera, Popular Culture, Popular Music, Sports, Trideo Shows, Vehicles

**Professional Knowledges (LOG)**: Accounting, Drones, Farming, Forensics, Foster System, Journalism, Law, Military, Photography, Security Design, Spirits

**Street Knowledges (INT)**: Area Knowledge (Boston), Bars and Clubs, BTL Dealers, Charity Shelters, Chop Shops, Fences, Fight Clubs, Mafia, Prostitution, Scrounging Locations, Street Art, Street Gangs, Smuggling Routes, Yakuza


**<a name="_toc218024792"></a>QUALITIES**\

=========================================
Qualities help round out your character’s personality while also providing a range of benefits or penalties. 

|<p>There are two types of Qualities – </p><p>- - **Positive Qualities** cost Karma but provide gameplay bonuses.</p><p>- - *Players can spend a **maximum of 25 Karma** on Positive Qualities.*</p><p>- - **Negative Qualities** give bonus Karma but impose gameplay penalties.</p><p>- - *Players can gain a **maximum of 25 Karma** from Negative Qualities.*</p>|
| :- |

***Note:** After character creation, some Positive Qualities can be purchased during game play, while Negative Qualities may be awarded to the character by the gamesmaster based on events that take place in game.*
### **Positive Qualities**
**Agile Defender (Cost 3 Karma)**: Speed kills, but quickness and agility can be the key to avoiding a speedy death. The character can use their Agility attribute instead of their Willpower attribute while using Full Defence.

**Animal Empathy (Cost 3 Karma)**: Characters with this quality have a natural knack for working with animals. The character gets a +2 dice pool bonus for all tests involving the influence or control of an animal (including riding), including Awakened species. 

**Ambidextrous (Cost 4 Karma)**: The Ambidextrous character can handle object equally well with either hand. Without this quality, any action performed solely with the off-hand (e.g. firing a gun) suffers a -2 dice pool penalty.

**Aptitude (Cost 14 Karma)**: This is how you become even better than the best in the world. Every so often, there is a character who can exceed limitations and be truly exceptional in a particular skill. With this particular quality, the character can have one skill rated at 7 at character creation and may eventually build that skill up to rating 13.

**Astral Chameleon (Cost 10 Karma)**: With the Astral Chameleon quality, the character’s astral signature blends into the background of astral space and is difficult to detect. All signatures left by the character last only half as long as other astral signatures. Any individuals assensing astral signatures left behind by a character with this quality receive a -2 dice pool penalty for the Assensing Test. Only characters with a Magic rating and capable of leaving astral signatures may have this quality.

**Bilingual (Cost 5 Karma)**: A character with this quality reads, writes and speaks a second language fluently. They can list a second language as a native tongue. This quality can only be acquired at character creation; selecting it gives the character a second free language skill during character creation.

**Biocompatibility (Cost 5 Karma)**: Something about the character’s body is exceptionally accepting of either bioware or cyberware implants (choose one). Not only are the implants not rejected, but they seamlessly fit within the body, having less impact on its holistic integrity. In game terms, the Essence cost of implants of the particular chosen type are reduced by ten percent. This reduction is cumulative with the reduction offered by the chosen ‘ware’s grade, if any. This quality can only be chosen for bioware or cyberware. This quality may only be taken once.

**Blandness (Cost 8 Karma)**: This character blends into a crowd; they’re seldom noticed and easily forgotten. They are unremarkable in every aspect of physical appearance. Anyone attempting to describe the character cannot come up with anything more precise that “average height, average build, average hair, etc.” Increase the threshold for anyone to recall specific details about the character by 1. Individuals attempting to shadow or physically locate a character with Blandness quality in a populated setting receive a -2 dice pool penalty on all tests related to the search. The same penalty applies if they’re asking around about the person based on the individual’s physical appearance. The modifier does not, however, apply to magical or Matrix searches. This quality decreases Notoriety by 1. 

**Catlike (Cost 7 Karma)**: A character with this quality is gifted with an uncanny elegance, a stealthy gait, and an almost preternatural ability to move without making a sound. They also claim they land on their feet when dropped, though they tend not to let people test this. Add a +2 dice pool bonus to Sneaking skill tests.

**Codeslinger (Cost 10 Karma)**: Ones and zeroes are practically a native language to a Codeslinger. The character is adept at performing a particular Matrix action (which is selected when selecting this quality) and receives a +2 dice pool bonus to that Matrix action. This can only be selected for Matrix Actions that have a test associated with them.

**College Education (Cost 4 Karma)**: The halls of academe are well known to your character. Thanks to time spent actually studying while at college instead of partying, the character can buy Academic Knowledge skills at half price (rounded up) during character creation. After character creation, Academic Knowledge skill ranks of 3 or higher receive a 1 Karma cost reduction for each rank.

**Cyber Singularity Seeker (Cost 12 Karma)**: In the Sixth World, many accept cyberware as a means to an end, as a way to augment their capacity. For most it is a trade-off between their sense of self and being more capable. For you, though, cyberware *is* the end. You believe that the more chrome you get, the closer you get to some sort of point of nirvana, of hitting a singularity where you blend man and machine to perfection.

The character gains +1 Willpower for every two full cyberlimb replacements they get (partial limb replacements don’t count), up to a maximum of +2 Willpower.

**Cynic (Cost 6 Karma)**: How many times does Mr Johnson have to screw you over before you just assume he’s lying to you? What about anyone else? You’ve been stabbed in the back so many times you’ve got little mirrors in your sunglasses to see them coming. You might be a downer, but no one gets the drop on you. How could they? You were expecting their sudden, inevitable betrayal all along. Anyone attempting a Social Test against you has a -1 dice pool penalty.

**Daredevil (Cost 6 Karma)**: Better to be lucky than good, when you’re living on the edge. A character with this quality is particularly lucky when it comes to doing the outrageous. Whenever the character performs an exceptionally daring action, they get two points of Edge back instead of one.

**Deep Resonance Connection (Cost 10 Karma)**: Technomancer only. Having known your abilities for longer than just about anyone else alive, dealing with these strange powers is second nature to you. You gain a +2 dice pool bonus when resisting Fading from any source.

**Drug Tolerant (Cost 6 Karma)**: The character has a higher-than-average tolerance for drugs (sometimes called Ozzy Osborne Syndrome). This could be due to a hardy constitution or a natural genetic mutation that allows for better absorption and filtering of foreign chemicals from their system. The character in question receives a +2 dice pool bonus to all Addiction Tests to resist addiction. They gain no bonus, however, for attempting to dry out after being addicted.

**Empathic Listener (Cost 10 Karma)**: Charming people always seem to know what to say. You might not be well-spoken, but you weren’t born yesterday either. A gut feeling, some honest empathy – you’ve got a little insight to make up for lack of social graces. If might not be pretty, but you can win people over by playing to exactly what they want to hear. Substitute Intuition for Charisma on Etiquette tests.

**Exceptional Attribute (Cost 14 Karma)**: The Exceptional Attribute quality is how you get to be a charismatic troll or the agile dwarf. It allows you to possess one attribute at a level one point above the metatype maximum limit. Exceptional Attribute also applies towards Special Attributes such as Magic and Resonance. Edge cannot be affected by this quality (but see Lucky). A character may only take Exceptional Attribute once.

**First Impression (Cost 11 Karma)**: The First Impression quality enables a character to slide easily into new environments, situations, groups and jobs. Whether infiltrating a gang, making contacts in a new city or wrangling an invite to a private meet, the character gains a temporary +2 dice pool bonus for relevant Social Tests such as Negotiation and Con during their first meeting. This modifier does not apply to second and subsequent encounters. This quality decreases Notoriety by 1.
