**Gifted Healer (Cost 2 Karma)**: A character with the Gifted Healer quality is particularly adept at one of Stabilisation, Diagnosis or Treatment. They receive a +1 dice pool bonus whenever performing the selected test, whether by magical or mundane means.

**Good Looking and Knows It (Cost 10 Karma)**: If you’ve got it, flaunt it! Good genes, good fashion sense or a good plastic surgeon have blessed you with looks that turn heads. The good news? You can often get what you want just by virtue of that pretty face. The bad news? They won’t forget that face any time soon.

You receive +1 Notoriety. Additionally, Memory tests to remember you receive a +2 dice pool bonus. On the bright side, you can ignore 2 points of negative modifiers on any Social test.

**Guts (Cost 10 Karma)**: The character with Guts is the one most likely to stand and fight instead of freaking the hell out. Guts gives a character a +2 dice pool bonus on tests to resist fear and intimidation, including magically induced fear from spells or critter powers.

**Hawk Eye (Cost 3 Karma)**: Characters with the Hawk Eye quality have exceptionally keen natural vision. They can identify a face a block away without binoculars or spot a spent casing in a shadowy crack at five metres. Characters gain a +1 dice pool bonus to their Perception Tests and shift all Range Environmental modifiers up one category (e.g. Medium becomes Short). The quality is part of the character’s natural eyes and is not compatible with electronic vision enhancements and/or cyber- or bioware augmentations or replacements.

**High Pain Tolerance (Cost 7 Karma/Rating – Max Rating 3)**: High Pain Tolerance lets a character keep delivering the pain even if they’ve had plenty piled on their own head. A character with High Pain Tolerance can ignore one box of damage per rating point of this quality when calculating wound modifiers. This quality may not be used with the Pain Resistance adept power, pain editor bioware or damage compensator bioware.

**Honest Face (Cost 5 Karma)**: Who, me? Whether you sold bad cars to old ladies or spent a whole lot of time looking in the mirror getting ready for Friday night poker, you sure don’t look like a liar, particularly when you are lying. This doesn’t make you look innocent – just without guile. Good for selling lunar real estate. Better for convincing the interrogator you really don’t know anything else.

Whenever someone makes a Judge Intentions Test against you, you receive a +2 dice pool bonus to the opposing Charisma + Willpower Test.

**Immunity to Iocaine Powder (Cost 4 Karma)**: You have developed an immunity to the colourless, odorless and tasteless Iocaine Powder, among the world’s most deadly poisons.

**Indomitable (Cost 8 Karma/Rating – Max Rating 3)**: Bodies and minds have limits, but some people have the will to push right through those boundaries. For each level of Indomitable, a character receives a +1 increase to an Inherent limit of their choice (Mental, Physical or Social).

**Innocuous (Cost 5 Karma)**: Sure, a guy can be bland and unmemorable, but it’s something else altogether to disappear into a crowd. You know how to dress mundane, slouch your shoulders, pull your hat low and turn the right corner. You can vanish into the masses, hiding in plain sight or approach your prey with the herd. You gain a +2 dice pool bonus to Sneaking Tests to hide in a crowd.

**Lightning Reflexes (Cost 20 Karma)**: Some people are just born fast. This quality provides an unaugmented character the ability to react with astonishing speed. The character gains +1 to their Initiative rating and a bonus initiative die. They also receive a +1 dice pool bonus for all Defence Tests. This quality is not cumulative with any other Initiative enhancement, be it technological, chemical or magical.

**Lucky (Cost 12 Karma)**: The dice roll and the coin flips your character’s way more often than not, giving them the chance to drop jaws in amazement at their good fortune. Lucky allows a character to possess an Edge attribute one point higher than his metatype maximum. This quality may only be taken once. This quality decreases Notoriety by 1.

**Mentor Spirit (Cost 5 Karma)**: Everyone needs some help in life, even if it comes from someone relatively filmy and insubstantial. Mentor Spirit means the character follows a patron spirit that guides them in their practice of magic and provides certain advantages and disadvantages to their natural abilities. Each tradition has a different name for a mentor spirit. Hermetic mages prefer the term “mentor spirit”, while shamans use the word “totem” for the spirit that they follow. While the names may vary, the way the mentor works is consistent. This quality is only available to characters that possess a Magic attribute rating.

**Natural Athlete (Cost 7 Karma)**: A character with this quality has an innate combination of physical fitness, spatial awareness and natural athletic or gymnastic talent. While they may not be a world-class athlete and may require training to achieve peak performance, they are in prime physical shape for their size and weight class. Add a +2 dice pool bonus for Running and Acrobatics skill tests.

**Natural Hardening (Cost 10 Karma)**: This quality makes the character’s neural structure resistant to feedback. This give them 1 point of natural biofeedback filtering, which is cumulative with a Biofeedback Filter program or a technomancer’s firewall.

**Linked with the Matrix (Cost 8 Karma)**: The character’s living persona can act as a master device of a PAN, with a maximum number of slaves equal to their Resonance Rating x3.

**Perceptive. (Cost 5/10 Karma)**: The devil is in the details and you see those horns regularly. This quality is available at two levels. For 5 Karma, characters receive a +1 dice pool modifier on all Perception Tests, including Astral and Matrix Perception. For 10 Karma, the modifier increases to +2.

**Photographic Memory (Cost 6 Karma)**: A character with this quality can often instantly recall facts, dates, numbers or anything else they have seen or heard. The character gains a +2 dice pool bonus to all Memory tests.

**Prototype Transhuman (Cost 10 Karma)**: You are an extremely rare, genetically crafted experimental post-human prototype. Unfortunately, this has its ups and downs. You were built better than a normal human, so you may pick up to 1 point of Essence of bioware (not cyberware). While you must pay the normal cost in nuyen for the bioware and otherwise follow all character creation rules, you do not incur *any* essence cost. So, essentially, you gain up to 1 point of free Essence to be used exclusively on bioware. These special organs were genetically grown into you from your inception – they are as much a natural part of you are your liver or heart.

However, the downside of being a rare, one-of-a-kind transhuman prototype is that, well, something is wrong with you. As part of this Quality, you *must* also pick one of the following negative qualities: Astral Beacon, Insomnia or Wanted. **You do not get the Karma bonus for this Negative Quality**. This quality can only be taken during character creation.

**Quick Healer (Cost 3 Karma)**: A character with the Quick Healer quality receives a +2 dice pool bonus to all Healing Tests made on them, including tests they make themselves and magical healing.

**Redliner (Cost 10 Karma)**: Any cyberlimbs you have installed are jacked-to-the-max, with safety limits disabled and performance overclocked beyond what the warranty normally covers, and that’s the way you like it. You receive +1 Strength and +1 Agility for every two full cyberarms or cyberlegs installed, up to a maximum of +2 for both attributes (sorry, no super centipede-man builds). The downside to pushing your ‘ware that hard, however, is that the strain is quite damaging. You lose three Physical Condition Monitor boxes per two full cyberarms and legs installed. Normally, every cyberlimb gives you one additional box, but with this quality, after two full limbs you end up with net one less box (i.e., -1 instead of +2).

**Resistance to Pathogens (Cost 4 Karma)**: A character with Resistance to Pathogens can fight off diseases more easily than other characters and receives a +1 dice pool bonus to those Resistance Tests. This quality stacks with the dwarf resistance to toxins and pathogens.

**Resistance to Toxins (Cost 4 Karma)**: A character with Resistance to Toxins can fight off toxins and drugs more easily than other characters and receives a +1 dice pool bonus to those Resistance Tests. This quality stacks with the dwarf resistance to toxins and pathogens.

**Resistance to Toxins and Pathogens (Cost 8 Karma)**: A character with this quality can fight off diseases, toxins and drugs more easily than other characters and receives a +1 dice pool bonus to those Resistance Tests. This quality stacks with the dwarf resistance to toxins and pathogens.

**Restricted Gear (Cost 10 Karma)**: Right place, right time, right friend or the stars aligned. No matter the reason, the character has managed to acquire or get a line on one piece of really hard-to-find gear they absolutely had to have. A character may start the game with one piece of gear usually unavailable at character creation. They do, however, have to pay any extra thirty percent for the item.

**School of Hard Knocks (Cost 4 Karma)**: The streets were this character’s classroom. Thanks to all the time spent trying to stay one step ahead oof the next guy, and knowing that knowledge is power on the streets, the character can buy Street Knowledge skills at half price (rounded up) during character creation. After character creation, Street Knowledge skill ranks of 3 or higher receive a 1 Karma cost reduction for each rank.

**Shoot First, Don’t Ask Questions (Cost 3 Karma)**: Your lifestyle doesn’t always you the luxury of checking all the facts before diving right in. As a result, you’ve honed your reflexes in order to survive and no longer allow yourself to think before you shoot; you just go for the kill.

Whenever you succeed at a Surprise Test, increase your initiative score by the number of total hits rolled on the test. This bonus only applies to the first turn of combat. If additional Surprise Tests occur later in combat, the bonus will trigger based on this new Surprise Test, on the next turn after that Surprise Test. This quality also reduces the threshold for quick drawing a weapon by 1.

**Speed Demon (Cost 3 Karma)**: Pushing your vehicle to its limits makes the hair on the back of your neck stand up, but in a good way. You feel alive, alert and ready to do anything. This increased intensity gives you a +1 dice pool bonus to Pilot Tests for a vehicle that is moving at a speed of 3 or higher (4 for aircraft). Note that your character must either be directly in the vehicle they are piloting or jacked in; the bonus does not apply to vehicles that are simply being piloted remotely.

**Spike Resistance (Cost 10 Karma/Rating – Max Rating 3)**: Characters with this quality have an inherent resistance to harmful forms of biofeedback such as black IC, dump shock, black hammer, etc. For every rating (up to three), the character gains a +1 dice pool bonus to resist damage from harmful biofeedback.

**Spirit Affinity (Cost 7 Karma)**: Available only to magic users, the Spirit Affinity quality allows a character to be attuned to one type of spirit. These spirits find the character interesting, are drawn to them and are more inclined to assist them. They may be reluctant to attack the character and if forced to do so they are likely to use nonlethal power. Watchers and minions to not count for this quality as they are constructed and are not summoned like normal spirits. Spirit Affinity provides magicians with 1 additional spirit service for each spirit of that type and it also provides a +1 dice pool modifier for Binding Tests.

Magic users may possess this quality for a type of spirit that is not part of their magical tradition.

**Technical School Education (Cost 4 Karma)**: All your schoolbooks focus on the practical and real-life working world. Thanks to time spent being formally educated in a technical school, the character can buy Professional Knowledge skills at half price (rounded up) during character creation. After character creation, Professional Knowledge skill ranks of 3 or higher receive a 1 Karma cost reduction for each rank.

**Too Pretty to Hit (Cost 3 Karma)**: It’s more about force of personality than actually being pretty – sometimes a character just has a presence about them that keeps people from shooting straight. The character can use their Charisma attribute instead of their Willpower attribute while using Full Defence.

**Tough as Nails (Cost 5 Karma/Rating – Max Rating 3)**: “Hit me!” is your favourite phrase. Each rating provides one additional box to either the character’s Physical or Stun Condition monitor. This quality can be taken up to 3 times for Physical and 3 times for Stun.

**Toughness (Cost 9 Karma)**: Characters with the Toughness quality shrug off damage more easily than others. Such characters gain a +1 dice pool bonus to their Body when making Damage Resistance tests.

**Uncanny Healer (Cost 12 Karma)**: This character has always been a fast healer, recovering from injuries with almost supernatural speed. Characters who embrace augmentation soon discover that it interferes with their unnatural healing ability. The character adds their current Essence attribute as a dice pool modifier to all Natural Recovery Healing Tests for both Stun and Physical damage. This does not affect magical healing or First Aid tests performed by others. This quality cannot be combined with Quick Healer.

**Watch the Suit (Cost 3 Karma)**: You paid good nuyen for a Starlight gown. There’s no way you’re going to let this clown bleed all over it. You’ve got the presence of mind and the little dextrous tricks to get in a tousle and still come out looking good. This prevents any Stun damage from marring your appearance. Physical damage will still draw blood and leave cuts, burns or worse that you can’t avoid. You never receive negative dice pool penalties to Etiquette tests for looking roughed up after a fight in which you did not take Physical damage and your appearance won’t suspicion that you were recently involved in an altercation.

**Will to Live (<a name="_hlk201588261"></a>Cost 3 Karma/Rating – Max Rating 3)**: For each rating point in Will to Live, the character gains 1 additional Damage Overflow Box. These additional boxes only allow the character to sustain additional damage before dying; they do not raise the threshold at which the character becomes unconscious or incapacitated, nor do they affect modifiers from the damage the character has taken.
### **Negative Qualities**
**Accident Prone (Bonus 4 Karma)**: This driving thing – it may not be for you. You have a talent for steering any vehicle you control into whatever wall, tree or other vehicle may be nearby. You receive a -2 dice pool penalty on any tests involved in directing a vehicle.

**Addiction – Alcohol, Mild (Bonus 4 Karma)**: A character with this quality is hooked on alcohol. This quality increases Notoriety by 1. Addictions get worse over prolonged periods of time without treatment. A craving occurs at least every two weeks. Alcohol has an addiction rating of 3 and an addiction threshold of 2. This level may be increased if the character has augmentations. At the lower end of the spectrum, it is easier to hide the effects of this Addiction.

If a character fails their Withdrawal Test, they suffer symptoms of withdrawal and must actively seek out and consume alcohol to find relief. While the character is suffering withdrawal symptoms, apply a -2 dice pool penalty to all their Physical-attribute-based tests. If the character succeeds on their Withdrawal Test, they do not suffer withdrawal symptoms and do not need alcohol until their next Withdrawal Test. They are able to stay clean for now.

**Addiction – Betel Gum, Mild (Bonus 4 Karma)**: A character with this quality is hooked on betel gum. This quality increases Notoriety by 1. Addictions get worse over prolonged periods of time without treatment. A craving occurs at least every two days. Betel Gum has an addiction rating of 1 and an addiction threshold of 2. This level may be increased if the character has augmentations. At the lower end of the spectrum, it is easier to hide the effects of this Addiction.

If a character fails their Withdrawal Test, they suffer symptoms of withdrawal and must actively seek out and chew betel gum to find relief. While the character is suffering withdrawal symptoms, apply a -2 dice pool penalty to all their Mental-attribute-based tests. If the character succeeds on their Withdrawal Test, they do not suffer withdrawal symptoms and do not need betel gum until their next Withdrawal Test. They are able to stay clean for now.

**Addiction – Soykaf, Moderate (Bonus 9 Karma)**: A character with this quality is hooked on soykaf. This quality increases Notoriety by 1. Addictions get worse over prolonged periods of time without treatment. A craving occurs at least every two days. Soykaf has an addiction rating of 1 and an addiction threshold of 2. This level may be increased if the character has augmentations. At the lower end of the spectrum, it is easier to hide the effects of this Addiction.

If a character fails their Withdrawal Test, they suffer symptoms of withdrawal (nausea, the shakes and headaches) and must actively seek out and consume soykaf to find relief. While the character is suffering withdrawal symptoms, apply a -4 dice pool penalty to all of the character’s Physical-attribute-based tests. If the character succeeds on their Withdrawal Test, they do not suffer withdrawal symptoms and do not need soykaf until their next Withdrawal Test. They are able to stay clean for now.

**Addiction – Gambling, Moderate (Bonus 9 Karma)**: A character with this quality is hooked on gambling. This quality increases Notoriety by 1. Addictions get worse over prolonged periods of time without treatment. A craving occurs at least every two weeks. This frequency may be increased if the character has augmentations. At the lower end of the spectrum, it is easier to hide the effects of this Addiction.

If a character fails their Withdrawal Test, they suffer symptoms of withdrawal and must actively seek out and engage in gambling to find relief. While the character is suffering withdrawal symptoms (insomnia, poor concentration and depression), apply a -4 dice pool penalty to all of the character’s Mental-attribute-based tests. If the character succeeds on their Withdrawal Test, they do not suffer withdrawal symptoms and does not need the substance or to participate in that habit until their next Withdrawal Test. They are able to stay clean for now.

**Addiction – Jazz, Severe (Bonus 20 Karma)**: A character with this quality is hooked on the narcotic, jazz. This quality increases Notoriety by 1. Addictions get worse over prolonged periods of time without treatment. A craving occurs at least every two days. Jazz has an addiction rating of 8 and an addiction threshold of 3. This level may be increased if the character has augmentations. At the lower end of the spectrum, it is easier to hide the effects of this Addiction.

If a character fails their Withdrawal Test, they suffer symptoms of withdrawal and must actively seek out and use jazz to find relief. While the character is suffering withdrawal symptoms, apply a -4 dice pool penalty to all of the character’s Mental-attribute-based tests and apply a -4 dice pool penalty to all of the character’s Physical-attribute-based tests. If the character succeeds on their Withdrawal Test, they do not suffer withdrawal symptoms and does not need jazz until their next Withdrawal Test. They are able to stay clean for now.

**Allergy – Adhesives (Bonus 10 Karma)**: A character with this quality is allergic to adhesives. Duct tape, glue and even band-aids and slap patches cause a strong allergic reaction. Swelling and a long-lasting rash that is discomforting and distracting is the result of skin contact with adhesives. This applies a -2 dice pool penalty to the character’s Physical Tests until healed.

**Allergy – Pollutants (Bonus 10 Karma)**: A character with this quality is allergic to common pollutants. In many places the very air causes a strong allergic reaction. Red and sore eyes, a scratchy throat and coughing as well as uncontrollable sneezing are common reactions to exposure to pollutants. This applies a -2 dice pool penalty to the character’s Physical Tests until time is spent recovering away from the polluted environments.

**Allergy – Soy (Bonus 15 Karma)**: A character with this quality is allergic to soy. After ingesting any product containing soy, they experience stomach cramps and extreme pain, sometimes coughing up blood. This applies a -4 dice pool penalty to the character’s Physical Tests until they vomit enough of it up, their stomach is pumped or it passes through their system. Skin contact with soy products will cause a rash and swelling and apply a -2 dice pool penalty to the character’s Physical Tests until healed. Furthermore, the lifestyle cost of the character is increased by 20%.

**Antipathy (Bonus 8 Karma)**: Your parents always told you to think about how others feel, but whether you want to or not, you don’t know how. You suffer a -2 dice pool penalty to all opposed Social Tests.

**Astral Beacon (Bonus 10 Karma)**: The astral signature of a character with the Astral Beacon quality is like, well, a beacon – highly visible on the astral plane. The signature also lasts twice as long as it would without the Astral Beacon quality and others assensing it receive a -1 threshold on their Assensing Test for gathering information about it. Only characters with a Magic rating may take this quality.

**Bad Luck (Bonus 12 Karma)**: The character is cursed – their own luck often turns against them. When the character uses Edge, roll 1D6. On a result of 1, the point of Edge is spent, but is has the exact opposite effect intended. This quality increases Notoriety by 1.

**Big Regret (Bonus 5 Karma)**: Mistakes happen. Sometime in the character’s past they did something serious that they regret; maybe they spent time as a bunraku puppet, maybe they were part of a major political affair or they were involved in the wrong corporate project, but it has to be something truly unpleasant (gamesmaster’s discretion). The character decreases their Social Limit by 3 against anyone who knows about their past. This could result in a case of blackmail if the wrong person knows the truth. The character cannot buy off this quality unless it becomes public, at which point they gain 1 point of Notoriety and must buy off the quality as soon as possible.

**Code of Honour – Warrior’s Code (Bonus 15 Karma)**: The character has a binding Code of Honour; it’s a matter of unwavering principle. The character maintains a strict sense of personal honour. This means they will not kill an unarmed person, nor take lethal action against an opponent who is unaware or unprepared for an attack or knowingly take an action that could kill someone who is defenceless. The character loses Karma each time the code is broken through your actions, or decision not to act.

**Codeblock (Bonus 10 Karma)**: A character with the Codeblock quality always has trouble with a particular Matrix action. They receive a -2 dice pool modifier any time they attempt that type of Matrix action. Codeblock only applies to Matrix actions with an associated test; it does not apply to actions that do not require a test. Characters cannot apply Codeblock toward Matrix actions they are never likely to take.

**Combat Paralysis (Bonus 12 Karma)**: A character with Combat Paralysis freezes in combat; this includes astral combat and cybercombat. On the character’s first Initiative Test, the character divides their Initiative Score for that Combat Turn in half (rounded up). In subsequent Combat Turns, the character may roll their normal Initiative. Combat Paralysis also gives the character a -3 dice pool modifier on Surprise Tests. If the character must make a Composure Test (CHA + WIL) while under fire or in a similar combat situation, the gamesmaster applies a +1 threshold modifier. This quality increases Notoriety by 1.

**Cyber-Snob (Bonus 12 Karma)**: There are augmentations and then there are augmentations, chummer. If you’re gonna stick a chunk of metal or hunk of flesh inside your body, it’s going to be nothing but the best! A character with Cyber-Snob will not accept any augmentations of a grade lower than betaware. A character must have at least 1 point worth of Essence of betaware-grade cyberware or bioware to be able to take this quality.

**Designated Omega (Bonus 5 Karma)**: It’s safer when someone else is giving the orders, isn’t it? That way, if it goes sideways, it’s not your fault. Or maybe you just don’t trust yourself to do the job right or you freeze under pressure. As long as you’re working support or moving with your designated herd, you’re just fine. If you’re put in a position where the team depends on you or you need to make a critical decision, you freeze up. You take a -2 dice pool penalty to all Leadership tests, whether initiating or resisting.

**Diabetic (Bonus 15 Karma)**: A chronic medication condition that requires daily insulin injections to manage. The character must daily succeed in a Body + Body (3) Test or their illness will flair, causing a -3 negative dice pool modifier affecting all tests. If the character keeps up with the necessary medical treatments (daily insulin injections), the threshold for this test is reduced to 1. The treatment costs 100¥/day.

**Did You Just Call Me Dumb? (Bonus 3 Karma)**: The character can’t resist camouflaging insults into well-spoken words. The character gets the satisfaction of feeling superior to everyone. Unfortunately, once in a while, people will notice and get pretty upset. Any Glitch rolled on a Social Test always counts as a Critical Glitch.

**Dimmer Bulb (Bonus 5 Karma/Rating – Max Rating 3)**: Maybe it was one too many hits to the head, maybe the character’s mother dropped them as a baby or maybe they never got into that whole “thinking” thing but whatever the cause, the character does not tend to shine in the mental arena. For every rating of this quality the character suffers a -1 dice pool penalty on all tests involving Logic or Intuition.

**Elevated Stress (Bonus 8 Karma)**: Years of having mainstream society look down on you has taken its toll, as has the long-term stress associated with it. You take a -1 dice pool penalty to any Addiction and Toxin Resistance Tests due to the strain on your health.

**Elf Poser (Bonus 6 Karma)**: The Elf Poser is a human character who wants to be an elf. They associate with elves as much as possible, talk like elves and alters their appearance to resemble an elf. Characters with this quality may undergo cosmetic surgery to get elf ears and elf eyes and they may successfully pass as elves and avoid any negative Social modifiers associated with being a non-elf.

Real elves consider Elf Posers an embarrassment, many humans think of them as sellouts and other metatypes generally consider posers to be pathetic. If an elf discovers the character’s secret, the elf is likely to treat them with contempt and hostility. An outed elf poser may also face stigma from prejudiced humans as a “race traitor”.

Only human characters may take the Elf Poser quality. This quality increases Notoriety by 1.

**Family Curse (Bonus 5 Karma)**: Your parent(s) liked their drugs. A lot. So did theirs, and their parents before them. To say that addiction runs in the family is like saying Lone Star officers enjoy clubbing punks. When making Addiction Tests, the character receives a -2 dice pool penalty.

**Illiterate (Bonus 5 Karma)**: Though literacy is not really necessary thanks to the advances of the Sixth World, most folks can at least sound out “See Spot run”. Whether because they grew up in the wild (urban, rural or otherwise) or just never had the opportunity, the character cannot read a lick. They can ask others, use an agent program or get software on their commlink to scan and read things aloud, but anyone aware of this intellectual deficit will look negatively on the character, reducing their Social limit by 1. The illiterate character also suffers a -2 dice pool penalty when working with computer/commlink systems and electronics other than their own due to their unfamiliarity with their iconography. Also, during character creation, the character cannot choose any Knowledge skill that may have required even the most minimal of reading and during gameplay all Knowledge skills that require reading cost double the Karma for the character until they learn to read and buys off this quality.

**Incompetent (Bonus 5 Karma)**: An Incompetent character possesses a total lack of knowledge or ability with a certain Active skill group – or, perhaps worse, they have some vague knowledge of the skills contained in the group, but they have neither the coordination nor the comprehension to come anywhere close to carrying it off properly. No matter how much effort they put into this area, they simply cannot grasp it – it would take a miracle for them to somehow, someday, advance to the level of “poor” in those skills.

Incompetent may not be applied to Language or Knowledge skills. The Incompetent character is treated as having skill level of “unaware” for all skills in the skill group.

In some cases, a Success Test may be required for tasks most people take for granted. Characters may not possess that skill group for which they have the Incompetent quality. If gear grants a bonus or requires the use of a specific skill in which the character is Incompetent, the character gains no benefits from the gear.

Gamesmasters are free to reject any choices that would prove irrelevant or exploitative in actual play, such as Incompetent: Outdoors in a campaign based entirely inside an arcology. (This should go without saying, but just in case: Characters may never choose Incompetent for any skill group that they are physically incapable of using. A non-magician cannot take Incompetent in Sorcery, Conjuring or Enchanting; a non-technomancer cannot be Incompetent in a skill that requires Resonance; and so on.)

Incompetent may be purchased only once. This quality increases Notoriety by 1.

**Insomnia (Bonus 10 Karma)**: A character with the Insomnia quality has trouble falling asleep and seldom feels well rested. Usually, this is only an annoyance. For runners, however, this can become a major problem when they are dependent on being able to rest at every opportunity to remain sharp. Insomnia can lengthen the amount of time it takes for a character to recover Stun damage.

Before a character rolls their Body + Willpower to recover Stun damage, the character rolls an Intuition + Willpower (4) Test. If the character succeeds on this test, the character is not impeded by Insomnia and the character regains Stun damage as normal. They also regain 1 point of Edge after a night of restful sleep. If the character fails, double the amount of time it normally would take for a character to recover their Stun damage. In addition, Edge is not regained after restful sleep for up to another 24 hours.

**Implant-Induced Immune Deficiency (Bonus 5 Karma)**: Cyberware and bioware users sometimes suffer from a number of health problems as the natural balance of their metabolisms is thrown off by modified organs and systems. The demands of their augmented biologies and the body’s continuous attempts to adjust to the implants can lead to decreased immunity to pathogens, poisons and other compounds. Characters with this quality suffer a dice pool modifier of -2 on all Body Tests to resist the effects of diseases, drugs, toxins and other compounds (including Physical Addiction Tests and Disease Resistance Tests). This quality is only available to characters with bioware or cyberware implants and an Essence of 5 or less.

**Lack of Focus (Bonus 6 Karma)**: Characters suffering from attention deficit hyperactivity disorder have difficulty focusing on a single subject for long. When making any Extended Test with an interval greater than five minutes and shorter than one day or if repeated simple tests are made within a period of time (such as Perception Tests during surveillance), the character must make a Composure (CHA + WIL) (3) Test each interval after the first. The character’s Composure dice pool is cumulatively reduced by 1 for each of these tests, like any other Extended Test.

Failing the Composure Test indicates the character can no longer focus and must take a break for a minimum of 1 interval, plus any other consequences that result. After the break, the character’s Composure dice pool is refreshed and the process starts over again.

**Lightweight (Bonus 6 Karma)**: On the bright side, this quality means it’s easy, and cheap, to get drunk. On the downside, it takes far less to get a person addicted to the various types of chemical drugs on the market. The Addiction Rating of any substance on the Addiction Table or any other related tables is 2 levels higher for the character.

**Low Pain Tolerance (Bonus 9 Karma)**: Characters with Low Pain Tolerance are particularly sensitive to pain; they incur a -1 wound modifier for every 2 boxes of cumulative damage, instead of the normal 3 boxes. This affects both Physical and Stun damage tracks.

**Motion Sickness (Bonus 4 Karma)**: Yes, there is a strong benefit from being able to move from place to place, but if your travelling comes with too much, well, *motion*, your stomach starts doing flip-flops. Any time you are in a vehicle that is effectively accelerating at a rate of 3 or higher or moving at a Speed of 4 or higher, you experience Nausea until the vehicle’s Speed or Acceleration drops. Once the vehicle movement drops, the Nausea disappears in (12-Body) minutes.

**No Man Left Behind (Bonus 7 Karma)**: You can’t leave a fallen comrade behind to be taken by the enemy. Whether they are dead or just knocked out, you won’t leave them to the wolves. Any time a team member falls (even one you don’t particularly like), make a Composure (CHA + WIL) (4) Test. Success means you’ve overcome this urge to save your fallen comrade (though you can still do so if you choose); failure means you needs to do everything within your power, up to and including self-sacrifice, to get your companion out of the hot zone and to safety.

**Oblivious (Bonus 6 Karma)**: The character with this quality fails to notice the troll in the corner with the Panther Cannon… even after they’ve fired it! They suffer a -2 dice pool penalty on all Perception Tests, including standard, Astral and Matrix.

**Ork Poser (Bonus 6 Karma)**: Influenced by Goblin Rock or over-hyped orxploitation trends, an Ork Poser is an elf or human character who alters their appearance to appear as an Ork. Various cosmetic biomods – tusk implants, steroids, larynx alterations, etc. – allow them to successfully pass as an ork. Ork posers are an embarrassment to many orks, but some tolerate, if not appreciate, the compliment behind the effort. This means an ork who discovers the character’s secret may either become very hostile toward them or be willing to let the character join the “family” – provided they pass an appropriate hazing ritual to prove their “orkness”. An outed ork poser may also face stigma from other humans or elves as “race traitors”, if those humans/elves harbour any prejudice against orks. Only humans and elves may take the Ork Poser quality. This quality increases Notoriety by 1.

**Reality Impaired (Bonus 5 Karma)**: The character is so accustomed to the Matrix and AR that they have lost any sense of what is real and what is virtual. The character tends to mistake real objects for AROs, and vice-versa, resulting in quirky mannerisms such as touching people in an attempt to call up information windows, ducking to avoid AR banners or trying to delete physical objects. This bizarre behaviour results in a -1 dice pool modifier to all Social Skill Tests when in the physical world (as opposed to VR or astral space).

**Simsense Vertigo (Bonus 5 Karma)**: Characters who suffer from Simsense Vertigo experience feelings of disorientation whenever they work with augmented reality, virtual reality or simsense (including smartlinks, simrigs and image links). Such characters receive a -2 dice pool penalty to all tests when interacting with AR, VR or simsense.

**SINner [Layered] (Bonus 5 to 25 Karma)**: There are four types of SINs that fall under the SINner [Layered] quality: National SIN, Criminal SIN (either Corporate or National), Corporate Limited SIN or Corporate Born. Individuals with SINs are required by law to use active mod to display their SINs. A SIN is required for all legal purchases. This makes them very useful things to have, so those who are SINless generally get by with the use of **fake SINs** just so they can participate in society.

**National SIN (Bonus 5 Karma)**

At the 5 Karma level, the character has what is called a National SIN. The character’s parents were legal citizens of a nation (such as the UCAS or CAS) and they have the right to vote, qualify for passports issued by their nation, enlist in the national military or work in the national government. A National SIN is required for any national security clearance or any form of national military career. A character with a National SIN pays fifteen percent of their gross income in taxes. They are also in no way connected to any of the megacorporations. The main drawback to having a legal National SIN is the character is in the system. The nation in the player character’s background has the character’s biometric data (DNA, fingerprints, retinal scans) on file and that biometric data is shared with law enforcement agencies through the Global SIN Registry. This makes is much easier to track a character should a job go sideways. Also, nations typically sell the personal information tied to the character’s SIN to corporations. Those with a legal SIN get nearly three times as much spam as those who don’t have a SIN or rely on fake SINs and the spam messages they receive are disturbingly tailored to their preferences (based on their buying and browsing habits).

**Criminal SIN (Bonus 10 Karma)**

At the 10 Karma level, the character has a Criminal SIN (either Corporate or National); their Criminal SIN replaces any previous SIN. At some point in their life, the character was arrested and served time for a felony-level offence and was branded a criminal for the rest of their life. They are legally required to use active mode to display their Criminal SIN at all times; failure to do so is a felony and can lead to re-incarceration. They are shunned by law-abiding society. Law-abiding citizens will, if they must, deal with a SINless character before they’d have any interaction with a known criminal. With their Criminal SIN, the character will experience prejudiced views, suspicion and/or open hostility from most people with SINs. They will often be denied entry to certain locations (high-end stores, car dealerships, museums, galleries, etc.) and will have difficulty finding legal employment. They can expect to be brought in and held up to 48 hours for questioning any time a crime is committed in their area. The judicial system in 2075 is more an assembly line than institution of justice. Suspects are treated as guilty unless proven innocent, plausible circumstantial evidence is often sufficient for conviction and sentencing has more to do with the judge’s mood than the crime. In this environment it’s likely the cops will be more interested in closing the case than solving any crime; they may try to pin crimes on the character with the Criminal SIN whether or not they had anything to do with it. Some degree of “adjusting” facts and “interpreting” witness accounts to support allegations is common; fabricating evidence, if only to meet conviction productivity goals, is not rare. Magic users tend to receive much harsher treatment from the judicial system than mundane criminals. If the character is a magic user with a Criminal SIN, they are registered with local law enforcement. They can expect regular – but usually not scheduled – checks to confirm their address and to ensure they are not using forbidden spell formula, foci or other magical gear. The nation or corporation that issued the Criminal SIN will keep close tabs on the character. If they fail to update residential information or appear in any way to be trying to evade their oversight, they are subject to arrest. They are also required to pay a fifteen percent tax on their gross income to the entity that issued their Criminal SIN. This quality increases Notoriety by 1.

**Corporate Limited SIN (Bonus 15 Karma)**

At the 15 Karma level, the character has the Corporate Limited SIN; they have somehow gained a position in a megacorporation from the outside. They may have been hired as a wageslave (or been the minor child of a person hired as a wageslave) or perhaps brought in by someone in the megacorp who saw advantage in their skill, talent, area of expertise or some other useful attribute. Under most circumstances, the Corporate Limited SIN replaces any National SIN. Their Corporate Limited SIN becomes part of the Global SIN Registry, to which law enforcement agencies and security corporations alike have access. Many of these Corporate Limited SINs record whether or not the character is Awakened. With the Corporate Limited SIN, the character can be gainfully employed by the issuing megacorporation as a wageslave, a low-ranking member of the corporation’s security services or an enlisted member of the corporation’s military. Though they could have a secret-level security clearance to perform their duties, they cannot rise to a leadership position, become an officer or be part of the megacorporation’s Special Forces (such as the Red Samurai). As a group, characters that possess Corporate Limited SINs are believed to either know something valuable about the inner workings of the megacorporation or have a skill set rival megacorps would want; as such they are considered valid targets for extraction, even if they are no longer active with the corporation. Characters with the Corporate Limited SIN experience prejudice and hostility from those in the shadows who are SINless. The SINless believe the corporations deliberately keep them poor and powerless so they can be exploited. The character with the Corporate Limited SIN may find themselves being personally blamed for their corporation’s actions – protesting they have no real authority and no connection with the actions in question usually does little good. To the SINless and neo-anarchists the character with the Corporate Limited SIN has sold out and chosen a corrupt and oppressive system over their own people. They character pays twenty percent of their gross income in taxes to their megacorporation.

**Corporate SIN (Bonus 25 Karma)**

At the 25 Karma level is the Corporate Born SIN. The character with this ID was probably born into a mega corporation or belonged to one when it achieved extraterritoriality. At least one of their parents probably had the Corporate Born SIN as well. They grew up in a corporation, their social involvement, education and almost every aspect of their life was managed by the corporation. Their skills and aptitudes were evaluated constantly and they were groomed for the career path to which they were best suited; their whole world was the corporation. Characters with the Corporate Born SIN had the potential and the opportunity to advance through the corporation hierarchy. They could have been a department administrator, a finance strategist, an agent of corporate intelligence, an officer in a megacorp’s military or even a member of Corporate Special Forces (Renraku’s Red Samurai or Ares’ Firewatch). With a Corporate Born SIN, they could have enjoyed top-secret clearance within the corporation and access to nearly unlimited resources. Then something happened. An unforgivably costly mistake, the machinations of a rival, a supervisor in need of a scapegoat – something pushed the character out of the corporation and into the cold and unforgiving shadows. In the shadows, a SIN that had been the key to opportunity is now a deadly liability. Most in the shadows see the Corporate Born as the privileged few, the aristocrats in the armoured limousines who look down on them, oppress them, exploit them and deny them their basic rights. If the SINless discover the character’s Corporate Born SIN, reactions will range from deep suspicion to violent hostility; serious injury and death are real possibilities. The character’s loyalty to their corporation is never questioned, which can be an insurmountable liability in a culture that works against the megacorps. Would-be runners have been killed for holding Corporate Born SINs. Fortunately, Corporate Born records are limited to the megacorporation that generated them. Files in the Global SIN Registry can confirm they have a valid SIN, but do not contain any additional information. Those with Corporate Born SINs pay a tax of ten percent of their gross income to their corporation.

**Social Appearance Anxiety (Bonus 3 Karma)**: Like the old flatvid once said, “I can afford a blemish on my character, but not on my clothes.” In the ages of style over substance, you need to look your best at all times if you’re going to compete. Problem is, you’ve come to depend on it. When you aren’t clean, coiffed and cutting, you become very aware of your own flaws, resulting in a -1 dice pool penalty to all Social rolls.

**Thrill Seeker (Bonus 4 Karma)**: It’s all about the rush. The character will always take the most dangerous and risky option in any situation if they don’t succeed at a Composure (Charisma + Willpower) (2) Test. There is a slight payoff, as the adrenaline rush provides a +1 to their Initiative Score for 5 Combat Turns (meaning that is how long the bonus lasts, not that the character gets an additional bonus each turn).

**Ugly and Doesn’t Care (Bonus 10 Karma)**: Fell out the ugly tree, blah blah, you’ve heard it all before. And you know what? You don’t care anymore! If people are going to judge you by your looks, then they can kiss your ugly ass. You’re not afraid to get a broken nose or a black eye. There’s nowhere to go but up. Reduce your attribute maximum for Charisma by 1 and your starting Charisma by 1 (to a minimum of 1).

**Uncouth (Bonus 14 Karma)**: The character with the Uncouth quality has difficulty interacting with others. They act impulsively, overreact to any perceived provocation and tend to do whatever pops into their head without considering the consequences (i.e. flipping off Mr Johnson, calling a drunk troll a “Trog” or responding to casual trash talk from a rival runner by punching them in the face). All Social Tests made by the character to resist acting improperly or impulsively receive a -2 dice pool modifier.

Additionally, the cost for learning or improving Social Skills is double for Uncouth characters (including at character creation) and they may never learn any Social skill groups. Uncouth characters are treated as “unaware” in any Social Skills that they do not possess a Rating 1 or higher. They may be required to make Success Tests for social situations that pose no difficulty for normal characters. This quality increases Notoriety by 1.

**Uneducated (Bonus 8 Karma)**: An Uneducated character is not mentally impaired – they just never had the opportunity to learn. Whether because they are their family were isolated squatters or were SIN-less or otherwise underprivileged, they were denied access to the education system. They have only a rudimentary knowledge of reading, writing and arithmetic.

Characters with the Uneducated quality are considered “unaware” in Technical, Academic Knowledge and Professional Knowledge skills they do not possess and they may not default on skill tests for those skills. They may also be required to make Success Tests for ordinary tasks that the typical sprawl-dweller takes from granted. Additionally, the Karma cost for learning new skills or specialisations (or for improving existing ones) in these categories is doubled compared to the normal cost (including at character creation) and it’s possible the character will never learn some skill groups belonging to these categories. This quality increases Notoriety by 1.

**Wanted (Bonus 10 Karma)**: It feels good to be wanted, or maybe not. Though most runners are probably wanted for questioning in a few cases, this is something different. The character may have a bounty on their head or a contract for their death. The character will have to frequently deal with someone coming for them or finding out about the bounty and using it against them.



**<a name="_toc218024793"></a>MOVEMENT**\

========================================
Getting from one place to another, especially from one piece of cover to another or closing the distance on an opponent, is important. Characters have three types of movement: Walking, Running and Sprinting.

A character’s movement for an entire Combat Turn (meaning total movement for *all* Initiative Passes, not *each* Initiative Pass) is based on their Run Rate, which is determined by metatype. Walk rate determines the farthest a character can move during a Combat Turn before they are considered to be Running.

It’s important to point out that “run” does not mean bolt as fast as you can; that’s sprinting. Think of running as a trained combat hustle or a jog, something to get you to another point quickly but still leave you able to perform other actions, albeit with a penalty. Sprinting is exactly that, running as fast as you can from point A to point B.

|**Metatype**|**Walk Rate**|**Run Rate**|**Sprint Increase**|
| :- | :- | :- | :- |
|**Dwarf, Troll**|Agility x2|Agility x4|+1m/hit|
|**Elf, Human, Ork**|Agility x2|Agility x4|+2m/hit|
### **Standard Movement**
**Walking and running**: The Movement Rates (Walk and Run) for each metatype are the distance the character can move during their Combat Turn. As soon as the character exceeds their Walk rate, they are considered Running until the end of the Combat Turn and incur any penalties or benefits of running. Running characters must use a Bonus Action each Initiative Pass they are considered running.

Characters cannot exceed their calculated Run Rate in a Combat Turn without making a Sprinting Test.
#### **Running Modifiers:** 
Characters who are running take a -2 dice pool penalty to all actions performed while running (except for Sprinting). 

Characters charging into melee combat gain a +4 dice pool bonus (making a net bonus of +2 when combined with the general penalty for running) when running into melee combat.

Characters making a ranged attack against a running opponent suffer a -2 dice pool penalty to their attack test.

Characters making a ranged attack against a sprinting opponent suffer a -4 dice pool penalty to their attack test.
### **Sprinting**
Characters may attempt to increase their running distance by performing a Sprint Action during their Action Phase. In this action, they make a Running + Strength [Physical] Test. Each hit increases the distance a character can move in a Combat Turn by either 1 metre (for dwarves and trolls) or 2 metres (for elves, humans and orks). Characters are allowed a maximum number of Sprinting Tests equal to half their Running skill per Combat Turn (rounded up). Sprinting characters also suffer fatigue if they sprint for too long.
### **Swimming**
Swimming is a Complex Action. A swimming character can move a number of metres in a Combat turn equal to the average of their Agility and Strength. You can take a Bonus Action to “sprint” with a Swimming + Strength [Physical] Test, adding 1 metre per hit or 2 metres per hit if you’re an elf or troll. Swimming on the surface of water or under it does not affect this rate of speed. As with the Running skill, swimmers suffer from fatigue after an extended time.

If you’re just trying to keep afloat, you can tread water. You can tread water for a number of minutes equal to the average of your Strength and Body rating. At the end of this time, make a Simple Swimming + Strength [Physical] (2) Test. Success means you can keep treading water for the same amount of time before another test; failure means you slip and take 1 box of Stun damage that you can’t resist.
### **Jumping**
Jumping is done from a running or standing position. Running leaps get more distance than standing jumps do, if you have enough room to get up to full speed. Make an Acrobatics + Agility Test, applying any appropriate modifiers. You jump a base distance of 20 centimetres multiplied by the total of your Agility and Strength and for every hit you get on this test, you jump 40 centimetres from a standing jump or 80 centimetres from a running jump in addition to. No matter how many hits you get, you can’t jump farther than your Agility x1.3 metres (net hits beyond this mean you did it with *style*).

For a vertical jump, it’s the same test, but with base height of 5 centimetres multiplied by the total of your Agility and Strength and for every hit you get on this test, you jump 5 centimetres higher.
### **Climbing**
The Acrobatics skill is applied to both *assisted* and *unassisted* climbing tasks. Assisted climbing is accomplished with specialised gear such as ropes and harnesses. Assisted climbing is easier and safer but requires more preparation. Unassisted climbing may be done on the fly, because you can climb without any gear. Climbing is a Complex Action and the number of hits you get on your Acrobatics + Strength [Physical] Test determines how far you can move vertically or laterally during your climb.

**Rappelling**: Rappelling is a gear-aided descent at near free-fall speed. This technique requires an Acrobatics + Body [Physical] (2) Success Test. So long as you have the proper gear and training, you can brake at any point in the descent, slow your speed and land safely. Rappelling expends a Simple Action, during which you fall at a rate of 20 metres per Combat Turn. Rappelling characters can increase the number of metres descended during that same Combat Turn by 1 for each net hit beyond the threshold on the Rappelling Test. If you take another Simple Action in the same phase, such as firing a weapon, you get a -2 dice pool penalty to both that action and the Rappelling Test. Stopping requires another Rappelling Test with the same threshold. On an unsuccessful test, you don’t slow down and may take damage if you hit the ground at speed.

|**Climbing Table**||
| :- | :- |
|**Situation**|**Movement Distance**|
|Assisted climbing down (rappelling)|20 metres +1 metre per hit|
|Assisted climbing upward|1 metre per hit|
|Assisted climbing horizontally|1 metre per 2 hits|
|Assisted climbing upside down (on a ceiling or overhang)|1 metre per 3 hits|
|Unassisted climbing upward|1 metre per 2 hits|
|Unassisted climbing down|1 metre per hit|
|Situation|Dice Pool Modifier|
|Assisted Climbing|+2|
|*Surface is:*||
|Easily climbable (chain-link fence)|+1|
|Broken (tree, loose stone wall)|+0|
|Flat (brick wall, side of old building)|-3|
|Sheer (metal wall, seamless stone)|-5|
|Slippery or wet|-2|
|Greased or gel-treated|-4|
### **Falling**
When a character falls more than three metres, they take Physical damage with a DV equal to the number of metres fallen, with an AP of -4. Use Body + Armour to resist this damage. The DV may be modified by a soft landing surface.

Falling characters drop 50 metres in the first Combat Turn, 100 metres in the second Combat Turn, 150 metres in the third Combat Turn and 200 metres every Combat Turn after that. Terminal velocity for a falling body is about 200 metres per turn.


**<a name="_toc218024794"></a>DERIVED VALUES**\

==============================================
**Defence Test**: Reaction + Intuition.

**Block**: Add the character’s Unarmed Combat Skill Rating to their Defence Test.

**Parry**: Add the character’s Melee Weapon Skill Rating to their Defence Test. Bonus die, such as from a relevant weapon foci, can be added to this test.

**Dodge**: Add the character’s Acrobatics Skill Rating to their Defence Test.


**<a name="_toc218024795"></a>CONTACTS**\

========================================
You are who you know. In the shadows of the Sixth World, this is truer than you might want to believe. Contacts are NPCs who serve as sources of information, goods and services that keep shadowrunners alive and well. Often, they can’t get chip-truth about what they’ve gotten themselves into from anyone else.

- Every character receives free points to spend on their initial contacts equal to their **Charisma rating x3**.
- The cost of a contact is the sum of their Connection and Loyalty.
- A single contact may have no more than 7 points spent on them at character creation.
- There are no limits on how many contacts the character may purchase.

*You can spend karma to improve or add to your contacts. Each point of Connection or Loyalty costs 1 karma.*

There are two Ratings that measure just **how useful** a contact is: **Connection** and **Loyalty.**

**Connection**: this measures the contact’s influence. The higher the Connection Rating, the more juice the contact has. A character can start the game with contact of a **maximum Connection rating of 6**.

**Loyalty**: This shows how much you can trust the contact. The higher, the Loyalty Rating, the more the contact is willing to do for the PC. A character can start the game with contact of a **maximum Loyalty rating of 6**.

|**Connection**||
| :- | :- |
|***Rating***|*Description*|
|**1**|Virtually no social influence.|
|**2**|Has one or two friends with some Knowledge skills or some minor social influence.|
|**3**|Has a few friends, but not a lot of social influence.|
|**4**|Knows several people in a neighbourhood; a borough mayor or gang leader.|
|**5**|Knows several people and has a moderate degree of social influence; a city councilman or low-level executive in a small-to-medium corporation.|
|**6**|Known and connected across this state; a city/sprawl mayor or governor, notable fixer or mid-level executive in a medium-sized corporation.|

|**Loyalty**||
| :- | :- |
|***Rating***|*Description*|
|**1**|Just Biz: The relationship is purely mercenary, based solely on economics. The people involved may not even like each other and they won’t offer any sort of preferential treatment.|
|**2**|Regular: The relationship is still all business, but the parties treat each other with a modicum of mutual respect.|
|**3**|Acquaintance: The people in the relationship are friendly, but calling them actual friends might be stretching it. The contact is willing to be inconvenienced in small ways for the character but won’t take a fall for them.|
|**4**|Buddy: There’s actual friendship here, or at least solid mutual respect. The contact will do out of their way for the character if needed.|
|**5**|Got Your Back: The parties know and trust each other and have for some time. The contact will back the character even in risky situations.|
|**6**|Friend for Life: The contact and character will go to the wall for each other, if that’s what it takes.|

### **Using Contacts**
Friday night socials and a beer at the local bar are all well and good, but the real value of a contact is what they can do for you, and while these things are helpful, they rarely come for free. There are **six major things they can do**:

**Legwork**: Legwork is chasing down the data trail and answering questions that may not be found on the Matrix.

**Networking**: Networking is all about putting the right people in the same room, getting them to talk and hopefully launching them on a mutually beneficial relationship.

**Swag**: You want something, other people have it. With any luck, your contact is one of these other people. You also might be able to sell them some goods you picked up while on the job.

**Shadow Services**: This is a special kind of favour. Contact who perform this kind of service have a job to do and they’re using their skills on your behalf for a form of payment besides the usual cash.

**Personal Favours**: This is also a special kind of favour. These contacts have power, influence or are in a position of authority. You want them to use that to bend the rules, turn a blind eye or whisper in someone’s ear a suggestion.

**Support**: These contacts may not have power, a job that can be exploited or money you can borrow, but dammit, they’ve got your back. Some may have some talent, a cool you that you don’t know how to use or maybe they just have a place for you to crash. More often, support contacts are the friends and minor contacts that are not necessarily a big part of the shadowrunner’s business but play a role in the other aspects of their life.
### **What does a Contact Want?**
Contacts don’t do things for you out of the goodness of their hearts. Everything has a price. Payment doesn’t have to come in nuyen, but it has to come. Maybe it’s favour trading, maybe it’s helping the contact satisfy a particular vice or maybe it’s supplying critical data. Each contact has a transaction type they prefer and if their price isn’t met, the character owes the contact. If the price isn’t paid in a proper time frame, the contact’s going to notice and there will be consequences.

**Cash**: For many contacts, the almighty digital nuyen is acceptable, especially in transactions for services and goods. A service fee would of course be added to the price of the item or service depending on the relationship the contact has with the character and the effort to find the item.

**Services**: More often contacts will offer their support, service or intel for a character provided that the character in turn does a job for them. The services a contact may request can be grouped into the following categories: shadow work, contact-related work and drek jobs.

**Barter**: There are contacts who do not use a bank or nuyen to keep their electronic footprint at a minimum, so they favour trading for goods, keeping everything off-bank and off-book.
### **Sample Contacts**

|**“Tincan” Oscar**|Homeless Beggar|**Connection:** 1|**Loyalty:** Player choice|
| :- | :- | :- | :- |
|Troll|Male|16 year old|Alone|

With a BTL addiction and a smell like beetles are using his beard as a cemetery, he’s not much to look at. But, for a small price, he’ll keep watch on a person or place for a while, hold on to something so the cops don’t find it or let you in on the latest gossip from the homeless. He’s pretty reliable, unless he gets his hand on another BTL chip – then all bets are off.*||||

**<a name="_toc218024796"></a>NUYEN**\

=====================================
- - Karma can be converted to nuyen at a rate of **2,000 nuyen per Karma point.** 
- - A maximum of 235 Karma can be spent this way. 
- - The character needs to spend the vast majority of nuyen they have. 
- - By the end of character creation, they may choose to hold onto no more than 5,000 nuyen as starting funds. 
- - Starting funds may be allocated to an online banking account linked to a SIN or on certified credsticks (see Equipment below).


**<a name="_toc218024797"></a>LIFESTYLE**\

=========================================
Some shadowrunners are in the business to right wrongs or to get revenge. There are a few in the business because they are utter psychopaths. For the rest, though, shadowrunning is mainly a matter of survival. They’re not willing to sell their souls to the corps and they know that begging will get them nowhere. So they scrape up money any way they can so that they can pay for the basics of life – food, shelter and maybe a little fun from time to time.

A character’s lifestyle represents the money they have to spend to live in the way they have selected. This can range from the homeless life of someone scraping up whatever food and temporary shelter they can get their hands on to those who live the lords of the sprawl, dwelling in walled-off palaces or airy condominiums that flaunt the extravagance the owner has earned. Most shadowrunners, of course, are far closer to the former than the later.

At the end of the night, every runner has to have a place to come home to. That place where they hang up their SMG, spells, deck or drone. A character must select one of the lifestyles below to be their primary Lifestyle – this represents the general affluence of their day-to-day life. They may elect to pay other lifestyle costs as well to represent maintaining separate residences for alternate identity or “safehouse” purposes but must pay full cost on all lifestyles they maintain.
### **Luxury**
**Cost**: 100,000¥ per month and up!

This lifestyle offers the best of everything: ritzy digs, lots of high-tech toys, the best food and drink, you name it. The character has a household staff, maid service or sophisticated drones to do the chores. They get by in their massive mansion, snazzy condo or the penthouse suite in a top hotel. Home security is top-of-the-line, with well-trained guards, astral security and quick response times. Their home entertainment system is better than that in public theatres and accessible from anywhere in the home. They’re on the VIP list at several exclusive restaurants and clubs, both real and virtual. This is the life for the high-stakes winners in the world of Shadowrun: high-level executives, government big shots, Yakuza bigwigs and the few shadowrunners who pull of the big scores (and live to spend their pay).
### **High**
**Cost**: 10,000¥ per month

A High lifestyle offers a roomy house or condo, good food and the technology that makes life easy. The character may not have the same perks as the really big boys, but neither do they have as many people gunning for them. Their home is in a secure zone or protected by good, solid bribes to the local police contractor and gang boss. They have a housekeeping service or enough tech to take care of most chores. This is the life for the well-to-do on either side of the law: mid-level managers, senior Mob bosses and the like.
### **Middle**
**Cost**: 5,000¥ per month

The Middle lifestyle offers a nice house or condo with lots of comforts. Character with this lifestyle sometimes eat nutrisoy as well as higher-priced natural food, but at least the autocook has a full suite of flavour faucets. This is the lifestyle of ordinary wage-earners or reasonably successful criminals.
### **Low**
**Cost**: 2,000¥ per month

With this lifestyle, the character has an apartment and nobody is likely to bother them much as long as they keep the door bolted. They can count on regular meals; the nutrisoy may not taste great, but at least it’s hot. Power and water and available during assigned rationing periods. Security depends on how regular the payments to the local street gangs are. Factory workers, petty crooks and other folks stuck in a rut, just starting out or down on their luck tend to have Low lifestyles.
### **Squatter**
**Cost**: 500¥ per month

Life stinks for the squatter and most of the time so does the character. They eat low-grade nutrisoy and yeast, adding flavours with an eyedropper. Their home is a squatted building, perhaps fixed up a bit, possibly even converted into barracks or divided into closet-sized rooms and shared with other squatters. Or maybe they just rent a coffin-sized sleep tank by the night. The only thing worse than the Squatter lifestyle is living on the streets.
### **Streets**
**Cost**: Hey pal, life ain’t all bad. It’s free.

The character lives on the streets – or in the sewers, steam tunnels, condemned buildings or whatever temporary flop they can get. Food is wherever the character finds it, bathing is a thing of the past and the character’s only security is what they create for themselves. This lifestyle is the bottom of the ladder, inhabited by down-and-outers of all stripes.
### **Sample Locations**
#### **High: Bonaparte’s Beachfront Condos	Cost: 10,000¥ per month**
Beachfront, overlooking the ocean with quality every step of the way. You have all the furniture and accessories you want, including the matching curtains. Your furniture is higher end and well-made. You have real art in your home, plus as much virtual art and décor as you want. You household drones are efficient and well-maintained. You eat on real china plates and drink from crystal wine glasses.

*Comforts & Necessities [5]*

Your home is beyond cozy, with enough space for guests or entertaining visitors at home. All your basic needs have been met and you are working on indulgences. Only exceptional situations interrupt your utilities.

You have state-of-the-art entertainment technology in your home and you have access to commercial-free or exclusive online entertainment. You don’t have to worry about budgeting for date night and can have a few standing reservations to exclusive restaurants or clubs. Your entertainment access and tech is enough to make your friends envious and impress your dates. Vacations last longer or occur more frequently.

*Security [4]*

Your home has excellent security, which deters all but the most determined and well-equipped thieves. You have a private security contract with a reputable firm and drones and trained metahumans patrol your property at all times. Your windows and doors have superior locks. Your Matrix system is well protected too, with IC running at all times. Your neighbours are likely to call police if they notice anything suspicious and the neighbours’ security teams will likely come as backup for your own if there are any problems. You enjoy considerable safety and privacy in your home.

*Neighbourhood [5]*

Revere (Rating A: 2D6 +3 minutes Response Time)

This suburb features high-class residences and corporate buildings. Police drones patrol the streets, scanning everyone for their ID and SINs, as well as contraband, and metahuman officers are quick to respond to issues. Neighbourhood watches will report anyone who doesn’t fit in with the right “look” to the police.

*Zen Den* (Asset)

Everyone has to have a place to show off their cool stuff, a place where they are surrounded by things that are fun and comfortable. The zen den is a room dedicated to the hobbies of the character. If could be a physical collection of vintage bottles, a trideo set linked to megapulses worth of trid movies, an immersive sports-viewing room and what-have-you.
#### **Middle: Troy Boston Apartments	Cost: 5,000¥ per month**
This 19 story high rise was once touted as a luxury apartment building but time and lack of maintenance have taken their toll. While still a very nice place to live, the building shows signs of its age and the year of wear and tear on the faux-hardwood floors, stone countertops and stainless steel appliances show in the scrapes, dents and dings. While the building contains almost four hundred apartments, they are all either studio, one bedroom or two bedroom at the largest.

*Comforts & Necessities [3+]*

Your apartment is comfortable and cozy with a full bedroom set and matching living room set. There is an AR window that allows you to change your view to one of a decent range of subscriptions. You have stable utilities, although the occasional peak-usage brownout still occurs. It comes with included parking in any space in the adjacent carpark stack, which is usually not filled to capacity. The apartment has a SOTA set of kitchen devices. Soy, krill and mycoprotein are architecturally “printed” into something that looks and tastes like close to the real thing. You can afford bottled water, you have centrally controlled appliances that work, such as a laundry machine and dishwasher, and you have mid-priced new clothing or items you bought on sale from Mortimer of London or Vashon Island. You can afford subscriptions to multiple entertainment sites. Nights on the town are more frequent and you can go to the occasional large event as well as an annual vacation.

*Security [3]*

Your apartment building’s security keeps out unwanted visitors and casual thieves. Determined thieves will have to work to get access to your place. Locks and in-home security are above average (Rating 3). Your neighbours are likely to notice any suspicious characters or loud noises and call security. Smoke detectors and fire suppression systems are standard in all apartments and homes at this level. Your Matrix system has an average firewall and will at least monitor itself for intrusions. There is a Panicbutton in the home connected to contracted police so you can feel safe and secure in your home.

*Neighbourhood [3]*

South Boston (Rating C: 1d6 x5 minutes Response Time)

South Boston is a pleasant, well-kept community. The public utilities, such as electricity and water, are reliable, the wireless coverage is up 24/7 and the neighbourhood has a standing contract with Lone Star. Police drones patrol the streets and you can go out at night without body armour. There are several popular chain restaurants to choose from, the grocery delivery serves are well-stocked and there might even be a park or green space. Neighbourhood watches are common and street crime is not. On the downside, this district requires all metahumans to enable public view of their SIN at all times.
#### **Middle: Atlas Arms 		Cost: 10,000¥ per month (this includes the Troll racial increase to Lifestyle costs)**
The Atlas Arms is an oddity: a classy establishment is a nice area, designed and constructed specifically to accommodate trolls. But not, just any trolls. It is marketed specifically to corporate bodyguards – the kind who wear suits and mirrorshades. While expensive, the comfort of having wide hallways, doors you don’t need to stoop under and furniture that doesn’t creak and feel like it’s about to break when you sit on it is considered by many to be worth it. In keeping with its target clientele, it also boasts a high quality gym with troll-sized (and reinforced) equipment as well as a boxing ring and sparring centre.

*Comforts & Necessities [3]*

Your rooms at the Atlas Arms have comfortable furniture, specifically designed for trolls. The walls are fully covered with wallpaper and include AR windows and wallspace programs and subscriptions. A BusyBuddy cleaning drone keeps things clean and your CHN (Central Home Node) is secure. It comes with a designated parking space in an underground garage. Soy is prepared on a multi-function soy processor and is almost indistinguishable from the real thing and you can occasionally splurge on real food like coffee on Sundays. You can afford bottled water, you have centrally controlled appliances that work, such as a laundry machine and dishwasher, and you have mid-priced new clothing or items you bought on sale from Mortimer of London or Vashon Island.

*Security [4]*

The Atlas Arms security is excellent, which deters all but the most determined and well-equipped thieves, including a round-the-clock manned security system. Your doors (front and balcony) have superior maglocks (Rating 4) and reinforced frames. The building’s security team will likely come as backup if there are any problems. You enjoy considerable safety and privacy in the Atlas Arms.

*Neighbourhood [3]*

Mattapan (Rating C: 1d6 x5 minutes Response Time)

Mattapan is a pleasant, well-kept community. The public utilities, such as electricity and water, are reliable, the wireless coverage is up 24/7 and the neighbourhood has a standing contract with Lone Star. Police drones patrol the streets and you can go out at night without body armour. There are several popular chain restaurants to choose from, the grocery delivery serves are well-stocked and there might even be a park or green space. Neighbourhood watches are common and street crime is not. On the downside, this district requires all metahumans to enable public view of their SIN at all times.

*Entertainment - Gym* (Asset)

Weights, treadmill, elliptical quadrilateral, gradient tricycle or whatever device is trending. All training devices and the space around them are troll-sized.
#### **Low: Grey Gables		Cost: 2,000¥ per month**
A squat, grey building that has seen better days but is holding on amid the urban decay. Conveniently, it is located at a hub of city rail, bus lines and the subway allowing for easy transport throughout the city.

*At the beginning of sessions that start after resting in this location, you must roll to resist 2S damage from the fatigue of this lifestyle.*

*Comforts & Necessities [2]*

You can count on regular meals; the nutrisoy may not taste great, but at least it’s hot. Power and water and available during assigned rationing periods. You own some cheap furniture purchased at a mass-market retailer. Still, your chairs match and you have somewhere to sit while enjoying your AR. You have a limited subscription to a virtual wall space program to decorate the apartment. There’s an open parking lot out the back where you can almost always find a space to park. Wireless coverage is available but at a low signal rating. You wear clothes from a second hand store or the sales rack at Kong Wal-Mart and you do your laundry at a cred-op facility.

*Security [2]*

With a maglock that deters crimes of opportunity and a bolt you can slide across your door, you can sleep (relatively) safely at night. The local street gang is in charge of building security and about as effective as their last payoff.

*Neighbourhood [2]*

Brookline (Rating D: 1d6 x12 minutes Response Time)

The neighbourhood has some community to it. Most people live in apartments or multi-family housing and even pay rent. This is a typical part of the sprawl, with dilapidated buildings, petty crime and little maintenance or public services. You can walk the streets during the day without being mugged and a sturdy lock should keep your things safe.
#### **Squatter: Pod Palace 		Cost: 500¥ per month**
Anything but a palace, this coffin hotel is cheap, basic and better than sleeping on the street.

*At the beginning of sessions that start after resting in this location, you must roll to resist 4S damage from the fatigue of this lifestyle.*

*Comforts & Necessities [1]*

Sure, the only space you can really call your own is a tube slightly longer and wider than you are, but it’s padded, dry and you can lock it against intruders. Plus, vending machines and shared bathroom facilities (with shutoff timers and no hot water) are available nearby. It’s not luxurious, but it has the basic amenities you need to live, and occasionally they’re even clean. Mostly of you clothing is Vendingwear (recycled plastic shredded and woven into fabric either avocado green or dirt brown in colour). But you do have one good set of second-hand clothes. You have enough food to eat at least one solid meal a day, but it’s unprocessed, unflavoured soy and you drink rainwater or second-hand bottled water with it.

*Security [1]*

The cheap lock is better than nothing and at least there are several hundred pods in the building so it would be hard to find you amongst the rest.

*Neighbourhood [2]*

Medford (Rating D: 1d6 x12 minutes Response Time)
