| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-4|Area|

A tiny, glass globe the size of a marble that appears to contain swirling mist. When shattered, a thick fog rapidly blankets the area proving dense and difficult to see through, imposing a visibility modifier equal to the Potency. The mist can be dissipated by temperature and winds.
#### **Painstone**

|<a name="_hlk212804858"></a>Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Essence|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Min/F|Drain: F-4||
This jagged-edged stone absorbs the pain of injuries that would otherwise be felt by the user. It is activated by drawing a drop of the user’s blood on the sharp stone. The user ignores the pain of injuries, reducing penalties from Physical or Stun damage. The activation test takes a dice pool penalty equal to the target’s Essence loss (rounded up). Each hit on the Potency + Force [Force] Test removes the effect of one point of wound penalties.
### **Using a Preparation**
When the spell is released from the preparation, it goes off as though it were cast by a magician. The preparation uses Potency + Force [Force]. If the effect is sustained, it lasts for a duration as listed in the alchemical preparation formula. There is no Drain in this because it was already taken by the alchemist; likewise, no Edge can be spent on the preparation activation.

The target(s) of a preparation must be on the physical plane.
### **Artificing**
Enchanting is the technique of tapping into the fundamental power latent in natural elements and imbuing items with magic that aids and enhances a magician’s abilities. The act of creating a magical focus is known as artificing. Unlike other magical goods, a focus is powerful, reusable and intimately tied to its owner. A focus represents a permanent and complex enchantment built up slowly from an arcane formula and finished with Karm. All foci follow the same basic creation process: first a focus formula is needed, then an appropriate telesma (the material item to be enchanted) is selected. After that the enchantment proper is created and finally the finished focus is bonded.

**Choose Focus Formula**: Designing a focus requires a complex arcane recipe known as a focus formula. Focus formulae, like all magical formulae, are produced using the Arcana skill. They are too complex for metahuman magicians to memorise and must be recorded in some fashion. You can buy focus formulae from lore stores and talismongers.

All focus formulae specify the type of focus, Force, form and tradition of the focus. The formulae sold by talismongers typically use “traditional” forms in widespread magical traditions – which is why a lot of magicians commonly create their own formulae. The focus formula must be for a Force that is equal to or less than your Magic Rating – you cannot make foci with ratings greater than your Magic rating.

If you’d rather create your own focus formula, you can design one from scratch. Researching a focus formula is an Arcana + Magic [Astral] (Force x Force, 1 day) Extended Test. Once complete, the focus formula may be used by any magician of your tradition to make the specific focus. A magician can translate a focus formula from another tradition into their own with an Arcana + Magic [Astral] (Force, 1 day) Extended Test.

**Obtain the Telesma**: Before you can create a focus, you need to acquire an item that matches the form defined in the focus formula. An object being prepared for enchantment in this manner is known as a telesma. Obtaining telesma may be simple or complex – if the formula calls for a knife it may be no more difficult than buying a blade from the local Weapons World franchise, but if the formula calls for a flute carved from the bones of a California condor, you might need to do some work to track down the item in question. Any inanimate object can serve as the telesma: a wooden wand, a jewelled charm, a weapon, an oddly shaped stone, and so on. The more unprocessed and natural the object, or the more work you performed to craft it, the easier the telesma is to enchant. For this reason, enchanters with the technical or artistic skill to do so often create telesma themselves.

**Prepare the Magical Lodge**: You’ll need a magical lodge with a Force at least equal to that of the formula Force, and of the same tradition as yourself and the focus formula. While you’re there, make sure you add some amenities, because you’re going to be in there for a while.

**Spend Reagents**: The reagents you need specified in the focus formula. Consumable reagents are considered spent at the start of the process, so they are used up even if you fail or abort the crafting.

**Craft the Focus**: You need to spend a number of days equal to the Force in the focus formula. You use this time to gather mana, hanging it on the telesma and working it into the material permanently. You’re actually working sporadically over the course of each day, so you can do other business during this time, but you can’t leave the lodge without ruining your crafting attempt.

At the end of the crafting time, it is time for the dangerous part of the process: invoking the power of the focus. Make an Artificing + Magic [formula Force] v formula Force + telesma’s Object Resistance. This counts as the culmination of all your work over the days, so you can’t use Edge for this test. Your net hits from this test, if you succeed, become the focus’s actual Force. If you glitch, you cannot resist Drain in the next step. If you critically glitch, the magic spins out of your control and rips away Essence from you – artificing is not for the weak or untrained.

**Resist Drain**: The Drain Value is the Force specified by the focus formula, plus 2 for each hit (not net hit) rolled against you in the Artificing test; the Drain is Physical if the actual Force of the focus somehow ends up greater than your Magic rating. If you’re still conscious after resisting Drain, you can spend an amount of karma equal to the actual Force of the focus to seal the deal and finish the focus. If you fall unconscious or don’t want to keep the result, skip the karma expenditure and start over (probably after you’ve healed).

The Artificing skill also allows you to assense a focus in a way that helps you understand its creator. Make an Opposed Test of Artificing + Magic [Astral] v twice the Force of the focus. You can use the net hits to learn about the aura of the artificer who crafter it. This can be attempted once a day per focus.
### **Disenchanting**
The Disenchanting skill allows the magician to temporarily disrupt or even unweave astral constructs.

**Disenchant**: To deactivate an active focus, make an Opposed Disenchanting + Magic [Astral] v the target‘s Force + owner’s Magic Test. You can do this from the physical or astral plane, though you must have line of sight to the focus. If you get more successes on the test, the focus deactivates.

The Drain Value for this test is 1 Stun per hit (not net hit) rolled against the magician; if the target’s Force exceeds the magician’s Magic rating, the Drain is Physical. If the target’s Force exceeds twice their Magic rating, then that item’s a bit more than the mage can handle and they cannot successfully perform Disenchant.

**Disjunction**: A focus can be destroyed and broken down into reagents. This requires touch contact with the focus. Breaking down a focus requires an Opposed Disenchanting + Magic [Astral] v the target’s Force (+ owner’s Magic if bonded and if the focus isn’t yours) Test. If you succeed in this test, the focus ceases to be. The telesma at the heart of it disintegrates and is unusable.

The mana released can be channelled into objects of the magician’s tradition, making them into reagents. Make an Alchemy + Magic [Astral] Test. Every success creates one reagent, up to a maximum of half of the reagents used in creating the focus. This process takes a number of hours equal to the target’s Force.

The Drain Value for these tests are 1 Stun per hit (not net hit) rolled against the magician; if the target’s Force exceeds the magician’s Magic rating, the Drain is Physical. If the target’s Force exceeds twice their Magic rating, then that item’s a bit more than the mage can handle and they cannot successfully perform Disjunction.

**Disjoining**: Put simply, disjoining is to Alchemy as dispelling is to Spellcasting. Disjoining allows you to remove the magic power from a preparation, making it into an ordinary object again. To disjoin a preparation, you need to have assensed the object and you need to touch it to make the attempt. Disjoining takes a Complex Action and you make an Opposed Disenchanting + Magic [Astral] Test v the preparation’s Force + the alchemist’s Magic Rating. Every net hit reduces the preparation’s Potency by 1. You then take the same amount of Drain as you would have if you’d created the preparation yourself.

There’s a risk to doing this – if the preparation has a contact trigger and you fail the Disenchanting Test, the preparation activates. Better hope it’s not explosive.


**<a name="_toc218024806"></a>SORCERY**\

=======================================
Sorcery is the art of shaping mana to create specific effects. You can use it to cast spells (Spellcasting and Ritual Spellcasting) or protect against or destroy spells (Counterspelling). You need to concentrate to cast a spell, but traditions may also include chanting, gestures, dancing or other actions to go along with it.

This specialisation of Perception is called Numinous Perception, which includes both the chilly tingle of astral forms and the “vibes” of noticing magic. With a Simple Perception + Intuition [Mental] Test with a threshold equal to the absolute value of the Skill Rating of the caster minus the Force of the magic (minimum 1).

Obviously, it a magician is throwing fire from their fingertips, you’re probably going to notice without making a test. But if the magic is subtle, then you have to pick up some dice.
### **Spellcasting**
Select a known spell. Select the target(s). Select the spell’s Force.

You need to be able to establish a link to your target – depending on the spell, you’ll need to be able to see or touch the target in order to establish the mystical link.

If you need to see the target, line of sight can be established with your natural vision, including using reflective surfaces and looking through transparent objects. Cyber- or bio-ware visual enhancements that have been paid for this Essence count as natural.

Any technological visual aid that digitises or augments the visual input for you (a camera, electronic binoculars, Matrix feeds, etc) doesn’t work – you’re looking at a generated image, not the light from the real target.

Spellcasting by visual targeting is subject to normal visibility modifiers. You can target astral targets when you’re in astral space (you’re not technically seeing them, but the analogy works).

Some spells can only be cast on target that you’re touching. You don’t need to see these targets, but you might need to make an unarmed attack to make contact with an unwilling target. Touching a target through clothing, armour or layer of paint is acceptable.

A magician in the physical world can only cast spells on targets that are in the physical world. Similarly, a magician in astral space can only cast spells on targets that are present in astral space.

If you’re using astral perception (or are dual-natured), you can cast spells on targets in either the physical world or the astral plane. Only mana-based spells work in astral space, even if you’re in the physical world astrally perceiving the target.

The Force of a spell acts as a limit on the spell. Higher Force spells are more powerful but cause more Drain. You can cast a spell at a Force of up to twice your Magic Rating. If the number of hits (not net hits) you get after applying the limit exceeds your Magic rating, the spell’s Drain is Physical instead of Stun damage.

Casting a spell involves some mental preparation and a Complex Action. Make a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test, including dice pool modifiers, for injury, sustained spells and so on. Any opposition roll or threshold you need to reach is listed in the spell description. 

**Rapid Spellcasting**: You can bypass some of the preparation, but it can take a toll on your body. Rapid Spellcasting lets you cast a spell as a Simple Action instead of a Complex Action, but with an added +3 Drain Value. If you decide to cast two spells Simple Actions in the same Action Phase, both receive the +3 Drain Value.

**Determine Effect**: Details on the type of spell are listed under each spell. Some spells require an Opposed Test prior to resolution, while others can possibly be dodged by the target. Note that the effect takes space even if Drain takes you out.

**Drain**: Drain calculation is listed for each spell; the Drain Value is determined using the Force and the listed calculation but can never be lower than 2. After casting a spell, you must resist Drain using the dice pool for Drain Resistance according to your tradition.

**Determine Ongoing Effects**: If you sustain the spell (that is, if you want the effect of a Sustained spell to continue), you take a dice pool penalty to all tests while it is sustained as noted in the spell description. You can sustain multiple spells, but the penalty is cumulative for each spell.

**Glitches**: A glitch on a spell might cause extra drain (generally a +2 Drain Value), invoke a different elemental effect than what was intended, hit the wrong target or any other bit of mischief your gamesmaster can think up. On a critical glitch, the spell could get away from you and cause all sorts of havoc or you might not get to resist Drain or it could go off in an unconventional and unpredictable manner that could harm you or your team – again, your gamesmaster gets to decide what happens.
### **Spell Characteristics**
**Type**: Spells are either Physical spells (P) or Mana spells (M).

**Range**: This describes how close you have to get or how far away you can be to cast the spell. The most common range is Line of Sight (LOS). Some spells require you to Touch (T) the target – if the target is unwilling, you’ll need to make an unarmed attack against the target.

**Area**: Area spells (A) affect an area rather than a single target. With a few exceptions, the area is a radius in meters equal to the Force of the spell.

**Damage**: If the spell inflicts damage, this describes the type – either Physical (P) or Stun (S). The Damage Value for the spells is listed in the spell or spell category description.

**Duration**: This describes how long the spell’s effect lasts. Instantaneous (I) spells have an effect that happens and then fades, while Sustained (S) spells last as long as you keep them going. Permanent (P) spells don’t fade or dissipate; their effect becomes a lasting, non-magical characteristic after you sustain the spell for (Force) Combat Turns.

**Drain**: This is the formula used to calculate the Drain Value inflicted by a spell. It is based on the Force (F) of the spell and can never be below 2.

**Indirect**: All indirect combat spells originate near the magician’s body (most magicians use their hands or eyes, but some use their feet for “power kicks” or emanate power from the entire body for a kind of an aura-throwing effect). So, you don’t really need to be able to see the target – you can cast these spells blindfolded or with artificial image enhancement – as long as you’ve got a clear line of fire.
### **Physical vs Mana**
**Physical spells**: When using Physical spells, the magician converts the channelled mana to energy and/or tangible material in the physical world. The tangible material is simple – energy or matter such as ice, acid, oxygen, heat, light, etc. This material is also temporary unless sustained, converting back to mana energy when the spell ends. Physical spells can affect both living and non-living objects in the physical world.

**Mana spells**: When using Mana spells, the magician can only affect living things with auras or astrally active entities (such as spirits or foci) even in the physical world. Mana spells can affect targets on either the physical or astral planes, but only if you’re on the same plane as your target(s).
### **Spell Categories**
**Combat**: These spells are quick, dirty and violent. The energy of the spell is used to harm, main or otherwise frag the target. Spell energy may be channelled directly into the target or it may generate external energy to damage the target from the outside.

**Detection**: These spells enhance the senses. They may allow the subject of the spell to see or hear over great distances or grant new sensory abilities. There are also Detection spells to sense the presence of other beings, magic, life and/or enemies.

**Health**: These spells affect the condition and performance of a living body. They can be used to treat or heal injuries, purge poisons or toxins and increase or decrease Attributes.

**Illusion**: These spells can mess with a target’s perception. They can be used to deceive, make things invisible, confuse the senses or provide simple or complex entertainments.

**Manipulation**: These spells are used by magicians to alter and shape their environment in a variety of ways. They can control the emotions or actions of a person, move objects, shape, create or channel energy or change a target’s form or appearance by altering its structure.
### **Combat Spells**

**Blaze**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3|Direct|

With a roar of heat, fire erupts around the target in an instant. It inflicts damage equal to your net hits on a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test resisted by Body + Fire Resistance. Roll an Armour Value + Fire Resistance –[Force]. The threshold on this test is the net hits rolled on the fire-based attack. On a fail, the target is set on fire.

The fire has an initial Damage Value of 3. This damage is caused at the end of each Combat Turn and the DV increases by 1 at the start of each subsequent Combat Turn. The fire can be extinguished with an Agility + Intuition Test, reducing the fire’s DV by 1 for each hit.

**Chain Lightning**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F|Aimed|

Lightning arcs into every target in the area. The area of effect is a radius in meters equal to the Force of the spell. The spell is targeted with a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] versus the target’s Reaction + Intuition.  It strikes each target dealing Force + net hits damage, with an AP equal to –(Force) and resisted by Body + Electrical Resistance. Each target suffers a -1 dice pool penalty on all actions and Defence Tests (but not Damage Resistance Tests) for 1 Combat Turn and an immediate Initiative Score reduction of 5. Drones or other electronics targeted also take Matrix damage equal to half the Physical damage (rounded down).

**Death Touch**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-6|Direct|

This spell channels destructive magical power into the target, doing Physical damage. The damage inflicted is similar to massive cellular die off from radiation or necrotizing fasciitis, but without the continuing effects. Since they are mana spells, they only affect living and magical targets. It inflicts damage equal to your net hits on a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test resisted by Willpower.

**Fireball**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F|Aimed|

The magician creates an explosion of flames that flash into existence and scorch the target(s), giving them the double benefit of causing pain and being intimidating as hell. The area of effect is a radius in meters equal to the Force of the spell. The spell is targeted with a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] versus the target’s Reaction + Intuition.  It strikes the target dealing Force + net hits damage, with an AP equal to –(Force) and resisted by Body + Fire Resistance. Roll an Armour Value + Fire Resistance –[Force]. The threshold on this test is the net hits rolled on the fire-based attack. On a fail, the target is set on fire.

The fire has an initial Damage Value of 3. This damage is caused at the end of each Combat Turn and the DV increases by 1 at the start of each subsequent Combat Turn. The fire can be extinguished with an Agility + Intuition Test, reducing the fire’s DV by 1 for each hit.

**Frost Grasp**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3|Direct|

Cold snaps into ice that grasps the target, typically binding their legs to the ground, although it could be used to bind an arm to a wall instead. It inflicts damage equal to your net hits on a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test resisted by Body + Cold Resistance. If at least one damage is inflicted, the target has a limb (or limbs) immobilised. The target may attempt to break free with a Complex Action, rolling Strength + Body against the net hits of the spell.

**Frost Shards**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3|Aimed|

The magician directs a flurry of icy wind and shards of ice at the target with a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] versus the target’s Reaction + Intuition.  It strikes the target dealing Force + net hits damage, with an AP equal to –(Force) and resisted by Body + Cold Resistance. This may damage gear as liquid components freeze, lubricants gum up and other parts become brittle.

**Ice Sheet**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Environmental|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F|Area|

This spell creates a slippery sheet of ice over the area of effect. Characters crossing the ice must make an Agility + Reaction Test with a threshold equal to the hits you score to avoid falling prone. Vehicles must make an immediate Crash Test.

**Lightning Bolt**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3|Aimed|

The magician launches a vicious bolt of electricity at the target with a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] versus the target’s Reaction + Intuition.  It strikes the target dealing Force + net hits damage, with an AP equal to –(Force) and resisted by Body + Electrical Resistance. The target suffers a -1 dice pool penalty on all actions and Defence Tests (but not Damage Resistance Tests) for 1 Combat Turn and an immediate Initiative Score reduction of 5. Drones or other electronics targeted also take Matrix damage equal to half the Physical damage (rounded down).

**Mana Ball**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F|Direct, Area|

This spell channels destructive magical power into the target, doing Physical damage. The damage inflicted is similar to massive cellular die off from radiation or necrotizing fasciitis, but without the continuing effects. Since they are mana spells, they only affect living and magical targets. It inflicts damage equal to your net hits on a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test resisted by Willpower.

**Mana Tear**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3|Direct|

This spell channels destructive magical power into the target, doing Physical damage. The damage inflicted is similar to massive cellular die off from radiation or necrotizing fasciitis, but without the continuing effects. Since they are mana spells, they only affect living and magical targets. It inflicts damage equal to your net hits on a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test resisted by Willpower.

**Mystic Blade**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Damage: P|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F|Aimed|

An arcane blade materialises just long enough to slice at the target, attacking with a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] versus the target’s Reaction + Intuition. It strikes the target dealing Force -2 + net hits damage, with an AP equal to –(Force +4) and resisted by Body + Armour.

**Sleep Touch**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Damage: S|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-6|Direct|

This spell channels magical energy into the target, causing Temporary Stun damage to render them unconscious but keep them alive. It inflicts damage equal to your net hits on a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test resisted by Willpower. The Temporary Stun damage is removed after (Force) minutes.

**Stun**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Damage: S|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3|Direct|

This spell channels magical energy into the target, causing Stun damage to render them unconscious but keep them alive. It inflicts damage equal to your net hits on a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test resisted by Willpower.

**Stunball**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Damage: S|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F|Direct, Area|

This spell channels magical energy into all targets in the area, causing Stun damage to render them unconscious but keep them alive. The area of effect is a radius in meters equal to the Force of the spell. It inflicts damage equal to your net hits on a Spellcasting + Magic [Force] Test resisted by Willpower.
### **Detection Spells**

**Clairaudience**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Passive|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-3|Directional|

The subject can hear distant sounds as if physically present at a chosen point within the sensory range of the spell. The listening point may be moved to another point within range of the spell as a Complex Action. A ward or mana barrier prevents the visual point from entered that area. The range of the listening point is Force x Magic in metres and does not require line of sight. While using Clairaudience, the subject cannot use their normal hearing. This spell translates only sounds within the subject’s natural range of hearing.

**Clairvoyance**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Passive|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-3|Directional|

The subject can see distant scenes as if physically present at a chosen point within the sensory range of the spell. The visual point may be moved to another point within range of the spell as a Complex Action. A ward or mana barrier prevents the visual point from entered that area. The range of the visual point is Force x Magic in metres and does not require line of sight. While using Clairvoyance, the subject cannot use their normal vision or astral perception. This spell translates only vision and doesn’t work with augmented vision. You can’t target spells through Clairvoyance.

**Detect Life**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Active|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-3|Area|

The subject can attempt to detect all living being (but not spirits) within range of the sense and their number and relative location. The range of detection is Force x Magic in metres. The net hits determine the level of the information provided. In a crowded area, the spell is virtually useless, picking up a blurred mass of traces of life.

**Detect Magic**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Active|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-2|Area|

The subject can attempt to detect the presence of all foci, spells, wards, magical lodges, alchemical preparations, active rituals and spirits within range of the sense. The range of detection is Force x Magic in metres. The net hits determine the level of the information provided. It does not detect Awakened characters or critters, astral signatures, alchemical preparations that have expired or already triggered or the effects of permanent spells once they have become permanent.

**Diagnose**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Active|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3||
Diagnose grants the subject information on the target’s general health and any illnesses, injuries or other mundane medical problems the target might possess. The net hits determine the level of the information provided. The caster must touch the subject to trigger the spell

**Low-Light Vision**

|Type: Physical|Range: Touch|Passive|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-3|Directional|

The subject gains low-light vision for the duration of the spell.

**Thermographic Vision**

|Type: Physical|Range: Touch|Passive|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-3|Directional|

The subject gains thermographic vision for the duration of the spell.

### **Health Spells**

**Ambidexterity**

|Type: Physical|Range: Touch|Essence|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: \*|Drain: F-3||
This spell allows the spellcaster to temporarily grant ambidexterity, handling objects equally well with either hand. The subject does not suffer the -2 dice pool penalty for actions with the off-hand. Your Spellcasting Test takes a dice pool penalty equal to the target’s Essence loss (rounded up). The duration is equal to the spell’s Force + net hits on the Spellcasting Test in Combat Turns.

**Detoxify**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Essence|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -2|Drain: F-3||
This spell is used to attempt to overcome toxins and poisons. Your Spellcasting Test takes a dice pool penalty equal to the target’s Essence loss (rounded up). Add the hits from this spell directly to the hits from the Toxin Resistance Test.



**Heal**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Essence|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: S-P|Drain: F-4||
Heal repairs physical injuries. It heals a number of boxes of Physical damage equal to the spell’s hits from the Spellcasting Test. Your Spellcasting Test takes a dice pool penalty equal to the target’s Essence loss (rounded up). The effect becomes a lasting, non-magical characteristic after being sustained for (Force) Combat Turns. Hits can also be used to reduce the base time for the spell to become permanent; each hit spent this way shaves off 1 Combat Turn (you can split hits between healing and reducing time).

Any boxes of Physical damage your target still has after any boxes are healed magically can only be healed by time and rest.

**Increase Reflexes**

|Type: Physical|Range: Touch|Essence|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -3|Drain: F||
This spell increases the initiative of a subject. Each hit rolled on the Spellcasting Test adds +1 to the target’s Initiative and every two hits adds one Initiative Die. Your Spellcasting Test takes a dice pool penalty equal to the target’s Essence loss (rounded up). A character can only be affected by a single Increase Reflexes spell at a time and the maximum Initiative Dice anyone can have is +5D6. The bonus does not stack with Initiative bonuses gained through cyberware.

**Resist Pain**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Essence|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -2|Drain: F-4||
This spell allows the subject to ignore the pain of injuries, reducing penalties from Physical or Stun damage. Your Spellcasting Test takes a dice pool penalty equal to the target’s Essence loss (rounded up). Each hit on the Spellcasting Test removes the effect of one point of wound penalties. A person can only be under the effects of one Resist Pain spell at a time (the one with the most hits).

**Stabilise**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Essence|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: S-P|Drain: F-4||
When applied to a character with a filled Physical damage track, this spell stabilises all vital functions and prevents the character from dying. The spell’s Force must equal or exceed the overflow damage already taken when the spell starts. Your Spellcasting Test takes a dice pool penalty equal to the target’s Essence loss (rounded up). The effect becomes a lasting, non-magical characteristic after being sustained for Combat Turns equal to the overflow damage. The spell must be sustained until the full time is taken for the spell to become permanent before the character is truly stabilised; hits reduce the time it takes by 1 Combat Turn each. If successful, the spell prevents the character from taking further damage from Physical Damage Overflow. 

### **Illusion Spells**

**Agony**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Realistic|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -2|Drain: F-4|Single Sense|

A favourite of mages going through bad break-ups, Agony inflicts an illusion of terrible pain on the target. Each net hit scored by the magician temporarily inflicts 1 box of Physical and 1 box of Stun damage on the target. It is not actual damage, only a measure of the effect of the spell. The target is affected the same as if the damage were real, with the usual injury penalties. If the target’s damage boxes are completely filled, they are racked with pain, unable to move or act. The spell is resisted with a Logic + Willpower Test against using the threshold of the hits on the Spellcasting Test. Once the spell is ended, the pain and damage boxes immediately go away.

**Agony, Mass**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Area, Realistic|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -2|Drain: F-2|Single Sense|

Mass Agony inflicts an illusion of terrible pain on targets with a radius of [Force] metres. Each net hit scored by the magician temporarily inflicts 1 box of Physical and 1 box of Stun damage on the target. It is not actual damage, only a measure of the effect of the spell. The target is affected the same as if the damage were real, with the usual injury penalties. If the target’s damage boxes are completely filled, they are racked with pain, unable to move or act. The spell is resisted with a Logic + Willpower Test against using the threshold of the hits on the Spellcasting Test. Once the spell is ended, the pain and damage boxes immediately go away.

**Full Sensory Illusionary Mask**

|Type: Physical|Range: Touch|Realistic|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-1|Multi-Sense|

The subject assumes a different physical appearance (of the same basic size and shape as their natural form) chosen by the magician. This spell alters the subject’s appearance, voice, scent and other sensory characteristics as well.

Anyone who might see through the disguise must first successfully resist the spell using the threshold of the hits on the Spellcasting Tests with an Intuition + Logic Test. This spell creates an illusion that affects both living beings and technological systems. It does not affect auras.

**Invisibility**

|Type: Mana|Range: LOS|Realistic|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-2|Single-Sense|

This spell makes the subject more difficult to detect by normal visual senses (including low-light, thermographic and other senses that rely on the visual spectrum). The subject is completely tangible and detectable by other senses (hearing, smell, touch and even taste, if it somehow comes to that). Their aura is still visible to astral perception.

Anyone who might be in a position to perceive the subject must first successfully resist the spell with a Logic + Willpower Test. Make one Spellcasting Test and use the hits scored as the threshold for anyone that resists at a later point. Even if the spell is resisted, the subject might remain undetected if their good enough with their Sneaking Test.

Invisibility affects the minds of viewers.

**Sound Barrier**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Area, Realistic|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-3|Single-Sense|

The spellcaster creates a perimeter of silence around the area of effect, (Force) in metres. Those inside the sound barrier cannot hear outside noises but can hear sounds within the globe and vice versa. Sound Barrier also affects technological devices, infrasound and ultrasound.

**Visual Illusionary Mask**

|Type: Mana|Range: Touch|Realistic|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-4|Single Sense|

The subject assumes a different physical appearance (of the same basic size and shape as their natural form) chosen by the magician. This spell only alters the subject’s visual appearance.

Anyone who might see through the disguise must first successfully resist the spell using the threshold of the hits on the Spellcasting Tests with a Logic + Willpower Test. This spell creates an illusion that affects the minds of living beings and is ineffective against technological systems. It does not affect auras.

**Voice From Everywhere**

|Type: Physical|Range: Touch|Area, Realistic|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-4|Single Sense|

The strongest kind of fear is fear of the unknown You project your mystical energy through your voice. Your voice seems to come from everywhere and nowhere specific in the room (or area). It leaves those who hear your voice unable to detect your location from the sound. While able to hear your voice, they don’t know where you are. You could be anywhere: even right behind them.

### **Manipulation Spells**

**Armour**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Physical|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -2|Drain: F-2||
This spell creates a field of magical energy wrapped around the subject’s aura that protects against Physical Damage. It provides Armour equal to the hits scored and is cumulative with other armour.

**Catfall**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Physical|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -2|Drain: F-3||
A spellcaster may utilise Catfall to slow a target’s fall to help them land safely without suffering fall damage. When determining the maximum distance (in metres) the target may fall without danger of injury, multiply the spellcaster’s hits by the spell’s Force. If the target falls a greater distance, subtract the maximum distance of the spell before calculating damage.

**Deflection**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Physical|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -2|Drain: F-1||
Deflection grants the spellcaster the ability to cast a spell of protection over a willing target. Every hit scored grants the target a +1 dice pool bonus for defending against ranged physical attacks. The effects of this spell are subtle enough to be discounted as a missed shot or poor aim (at least at first).

**Light**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Environmental|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -1|Drain: F-4|Area|

This spell creates a mobile point of light, illuminating a radius around it equal to the spell’s Force in meters. This spell cannot be used to blind a target, but it offsets darkness visibility modifiers. Each hit on the Spellcasting Test counters a -1 dice pool penalty due to light conditions.

**Lock**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Physical|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Sustain -2|Drain: F-2||
Lock allows the spellcaster to telekinetically hold a door (or portal, hatch, closure or similar blockage) closed with a Strength equal to the Force. Opening the portal requires an Opposed Test between Strength and the spell’s Force.

**Mist**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Environmental|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3|Area|

Mist creates a thick fog that blankets the entire area of effect. The mist is dense and difficult to see through, imposing a visibility modifier equal to the hits scored by the caster. The mist dissipates quickly based on the surrounding temperature and winds. Generally speaking, this means the vision modifier is reduced by 1 per Combat Turn, modified by the temperature and winds.

**Sterilise**

|Type: Physical|Range: LOS|Environmental|
| :- | :- | :- |
|Duration: Instant|Drain: F-3|Area|

This spell allows a spellcaster to kill all bacteria (and other microorganisms) and destroy organic material such as skin flakes, stray hairs and spilled blood. Material affected by this spell cannot be used as a material link. Because the spell does not affect biomaterial attached to a living being, it does not kill the various helpful and harmful microorganisms living inside a creature. Each hit scored by the caster inflicts a -1 dice pool penalty to any skill tests made to collect and use sterilised biomaterial for forensics purposes. Shadowrunners often employ this spell to eliminate incriminating trace evidence, especially if blood has been spilled. The area sterilised equals the caster’s Magic Rating in cubic metres.

### **Counterspelling**
Counterspelling offers the magician two benefits: spell defence and dispelling. The Counterspelling skill does not work against spirits, critter powers or alchemical preparations.

**Spell Defence**: Spell Defence is used against hostile spells cast at you or at targets that are within your line of sight that you decide to protect with spell defence. 

*Spell Shielding*: As a Bonus Action, select a number of people (including yourself if you desire) within 1 metre per point of Counterspelling skill. Dice equal to your Counterspelling skill are added to the defence test against spells of everyone you’re covering. This lasts until the end of the Combat Turn.

*Spellbreaking*: As an Interrupt Action that reduces your Initiative Score by 5, when a spellcaster is casting a spell. Make a Counterspelling + Magic [Astral] Test; each hit reduces the hits of the opposing spellcaster’s spellcasting test.

**Dispelling**: Dispelling is used to counter a sustained spell. A Dispelling Test is the dispeller’s Counterspelling + Magic [Astral] against the spell’s Force + caster’s Magic. Every net hit reduces the number of hits the caster had in casting the spell. This may reduce the effectiveness of the spell. If the spell is reduced to 0 net hits, the spell ends completely. Regardless of how it goes, you take the Drain from the spell as if you had cast it – Physical if the spell’s Force was higher than your Magic rating, Stun otherwise.

**Ritual Drain**: A ritual can be drained of power if it contains the “Spell” keyword and is ongoing (sustained or with a duration). Make an Opposed Counterspelling + Magic [Astral] Test against a dice pool equal to the sum of the Force of the spell and the total of the Magic Ratings of all the ritual’s participants. Every net hit you get reduces the net hits from the ritual’s sealing step by 1. You take drain equal to twice the hits (not net hits) on the opposing test. The Drain from draining a ritual is Stun unless the ritual’s Force is greater than your Magic rating, in which case the Drain is Physical.
### **Ritual Spellcasting**
While spellcasting is the quick manipulation of mana, ritual spellcasting shapes mana over a longer period of time. More time allows you to manipulate mana in ways that normal spellcasting won’t allow. Rituals can be performed by either one person or a group.

**Choose Ritual Leader**: Each ritual must have a leader who know the ritual being performed and can complete the last step, which seals the ritual. The participants do not need to have learned the ritual; they simply must be willing to take part. All effects from the ritual have the leader’s **astral signature**. Participants who are not of the same tradition as the leader suffer a minimum of a -2 dice pool penalty on all actions for the ritual. If you’re casting a ritual all alone, you’re the leader.

**Choose Ritual**: The leader must then choose the ritual to perform. If required, the leader also chooses the spell that will be included as part of the ritual. If the ritual requires knowledge of a spell or spell category, only the leader needs to know them.

**Choose the Force**: The Force of the ritual determines not only its general power, but also the Force of any spell woven into it.

**Set Up the Foundation**: A ritual must be performed in a magical lodge appropriate to the leader’s tradition, which is referred to as the foundation for the ritual. This can be a permanent magical lodge, or a temporary one. The Force of the lodge must equal or exceed the Force of the ritual to be cast. Once the lodge is active, no participant (except a spotter, if the ritual calls for one) may leave the foundation until the ritual is complete without causing the ritual to fail.

**Perform the Ritual**: The duration of this step is specific to each ritual (see their descriptions), but is almost always based on the ritual’s Force.

**Seal the Ritual**: The final step in any ritual is sealing it, which completes the ritual. The leader makes a Ritual Spellcasting + Magic [Force] v (Force x2) test, with a Teamwork Test from each of the participants. Each ritual’s description explains how the net hits from the sealing step are used, if at all.

After the spell effect goes off, each participant also takes Drain equal to twice the number of hits (not net hits) on the defence side of the Ritual Spellcasting Test (minimum 2). If the number of hits the leader got on their Teamwork Test was higher than their Magic rating, this drain is Physical; otherwise, it’s Stun.
### **Ritual Failure**
There are a number of things that could cause a ritual to fail prematurely. If a participant leaves the foundation before the ritual is sealed, the ritual fails. If the leader is incapacitated (or killed) before the ritual is sealed, the ritual fails. If the foundation is disrupted or broken before the ritual is sealed, the ritual fails.

When a ritual fails, every participant immediately suffers Drain. Make a Force x 2 Test, as though the spell had actually been cast; the Drain is equal to twice the number of hits (not net hits) on this test in Stun damage.

**Glitches**: A glitch on a ritual in any step could result in extra Drain (e.g. +2 Drain Value), an increase of 2 to the Force resisting completion of the spell or the leader being forced to seal the ritual on their own. On a critical glitch, anything goes (prepare to put down that accidentally summoned demon, find that your astral form has been bound into the ritual focus item, find your healing circle is really an astral gateway and everybody just got dumped on some metaplane or something equally unpleasant).
### **Anchored Rituals**
An anchored ritual is anchored to a physical object (a tree or doorway, for example) or symbol/s of mystical significance to the tradition (written in ink, paint, blood, etch marks, etc.) that serves as the ritual’s focal point. This could be something used specifically for the ritual. While some anchored rituals create an effect that is simply a sphere expanding from the central focus, other allow the ritualist to shape the area of effect with tokens that resonate with the anchoring object or symbols mystically tied to the central symbol that allow the area to fit within the confines of a building or even certain rooms within a building. The anchor cannot be moved relative to the Gaiasphere (the planet) during the duration of the ritual’s effect or the ritual collapses and the effect ends early.
### **Rituals**
These are rituals that you can learn and cast. 

**Alarm Ward**

Alarm Wards alert their creator when a physical form has entered or crossed any area they are set to guard (with a size threshold to prevent a mosquito from triggering the Alarm Ward. Alarm Wards are tenuous, designed to be as unobtrusive as possible so as to blend into the local astral space and allow any intruder to pass through, (hopefully) unaware they have been detected.

*Keywords*: Anchored

*Effect*: Astral entities must make an Assensing + Intuition [Astral] (3) Test to notice the ward before passing through it. Those on the physical realm or using spells like Clairvoyance need to succeed at a Perception Test (5) to notice the ritual marking and anchor of the ward. This is to notice the “magical markings” but not understand their intent. That is a standard Arcane Knowledge Test.

*Area*: Either a sphere with a radius in metres equal to fifty cubic metres times the sum of the participants’ Magic Ratings and the net hits from the sealing step or a space with the same area or smaller.

*Duration*: 1 hour (at one hit), which is doubled for each additional net hit from the sealing step of the ritual.

*Ritual Time*: (Force) hours to perform.

**Astral Alarm Ward**

Astral Alarm Wards alert their creator when a spell or astral form has entered or crossed any area they are set to guard. Astral Alarm Wards are tenuous, designed to be as unobtrusive as possible so as to blend into the local astral space and allow any intruder to pass through, (hopefully) unaware they have been detected.

*Keywords*: Anchored

*Effect*: Astral entities must make an Assensing + Intuition [Astral] (3) Test to notice the ward before passing through it. Those on the physical realm or using spells like Clairvoyance need to succeed at a Perception Test (5) to notice the ritual marking and anchor of the ward. This is to notice the “magical markings” but not understand their intent. That is a standard Arcane Knowledge Test.

*Area*: Either a sphere with a radius in metres equal to fifty cubic metres times the sum of the participants’ Magic Ratings and the net hits from the sealing step or a space with the same area or smaller.

*Duration*: 1 hour (at one hit), which is doubled for each additional net hit from the sealing step of the ritual.

*Ritual Time*: (Force) hours to perform.

**Circle of Protection**

The circle of protection is a small astral and physical barrier. The barrier is dual-natured. Anyone or anything within the barrier is protected from outside physical objects and magical attacks. If something crosses the barrier from the inside, then the circle ends.

*Keywords*: Anchored

*Effect*: The circle acts as a combination of physical barrier and mana barrier with a Force equal to the Force of the ritual.

*Area*: Even though it’s called a circle, it creates a sphere around the anchor that has a radius in metres equal to the leader’s Magic Rating.

*Duration*: 1 hour per net hit from the sealing step of the ritual.

*Ritual Time*: (Force) hours to perform.

**Dread Domain**

This ritual creates an area of that mystically broadcasts feelings of imminent danger, fear and unease to any living being who enters the domain. They simultaneously feel chilled and nervous. Their hackles rise and they feel slightly panicked. It does not affect the ritualist/s (however, other allies may not be excluded from the effects).

*Keywords*: Anchored, Spell

*Effect*: Characters that fail to resist suffer a -1 dice pool modifier to all actions for each net hit on the Sealing Test as long as they remain in the area of effect.

*Area*: Either a sphere with a radius in metres equal to fifty cubic metres times the sum of the participants’ Magic Ratings and the net hits from the sealing step or a space with the same area or smaller.

*Duration*: 1 hour per net hit from the sealing step of the ritual.

*Ritual Time*: (Force) hours to perform.

**Safe Landing Zone**

This ritual creates an area that slows the fall of those who enter it, helping them to land safely without suffering falling damage.

*Keywords*: Anchored, Spell

*Effect*: When calculating the maximum distance (in metres) a character has fallen without danger of injury, multiply the ritualist’s hits by the ritual’s Force. If the target falls a greater distance, subtract the maximum distance of the ritual before calculating damage.

*Area*: Either a sphere with a radius in metres equal to fifty cubic metres times the sum of the participants’ Magic Ratings and the net hits from the sealing step or a space with the same area or smaller.

*Duration*: 1 hour per net hit from the sealing step of the ritual.

*Ritual Time*: (Force) hours to perform.

**Silence Zone**

This ritual creates a perimeter of silence. Those inside the zone cannot hear outside noises but can hear sounds within the zone and vice versa. Only sounds crossing the zone are affected. It also affects technological devices, infrasound and ultrasound.

*Keywords*: Anchored, Spell

*Effect*: Perimeter of silence.

*Area*: Either a sphere with a radius in metres equal to fifty cubic metres times the sum of the participants’ Magic Ratings and the net hits from the sealing step or a space with the same area or smaller.

*Duration*: 1 hour (at one hit), which is doubled for each additional net hit from the sealing step of the ritual.

*Ritual Time*: (Force) hours to perform.

**Shadowed Domain**

This ritual creates an area of mystical shadows and darkness that restricts vision (does not affect thermographic vision).

*Keywords*: Anchored, Spell

*Effect*: 2 Force for Partial Light, 4 Force for Dim Light and 6 Force for Total Darkness.

*Area*: Either a sphere with a radius in metres equal to fifty cubic metres times the sum of the participants’ Magic Ratings and the net hits from the sealing step or a space with the same area or smaller.

*Duration*: 1 hour (at one hit), which is doubled for each additional net hit from the sealing step of the ritual.

*Ritual Time*: (Force) hours to perform.

**Ward**

The ward is a basic ritual, taught to many magicians that creates an astral barrier.

*Keywords*: Anchored

*Effect*: It creates an astral barrier with a Force equal to the Force of the ritual.

*Area*: Either a sphere with a radius in metres equal to fifty cubic metres times the sum of the participants’ Magic Ratings and the net hits from the sealing step or a space with the same area or smaller.

*Duration*: Weeks equal to the net hits from the sealing of the ritual.

*Ritual Time*: (Force) hours to perform.

**Watcher**

Watchers are like spirits, but in actuality are entities born from the ritual leader’s own mind rather than the metaplanes. They are a creation of mana, woven with the personalities of the ritual participants. A watcher can speak any language its creators (which include the leader and participants) can speak. A watcher is bound only to the leader of the ritual and follows their orders. Unlike spirits, watchers do not have a telepathic link with the leader. They must communicate with words to pass on a message. A watcher is a minion. A character can’t have more minions at a time that their Charisma rating. A leader can dismiss a watcher bound to them as a Bonus Action. Watchers cannot be banished or counterspelled.

*Keywords*: Minion

*Duration*: Hours equal to Force times the net hits on the sealing test

*Ritual Time*: (Force) minutes to perform.

*Watcher*

|**B**|**A**|**R**|**S**|**W**|**L**|**I**|**C**|**Powers**||
| :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: | :- |
|**\***|\*|\*|\*|F/2|F/2|F/2|F/2|<p>**Astral Form**: Only astral attacks or mana spells/powers may hurt a watcher. Watchers can only affect dual-natured beings or those on the astral plane.</p><p>**Manifest**: Watchers may manifest (or unmanifest) as a Complex Action.</p><p>**Search**: A watcher may search for a target but must have seen the target (or an image of it) before the search begins. A watcher may search in the astral plane without manifesting, even if the target is in the physical world.</p><p>It must succeed at a Force + Intuition (5, 10 minutes) Extended Test.</p><p>**Sapience**: Watchers are self-aware and capable of making their own choices while following orders.</p>||
|**Astral Initiative**|(F x2) + 1D6|||||||||
|**Skills**|<p>Assensing</p><p>Astral Combat</p><p>Perception</p>|<p>F+I</p><p>F+W</p><p>F+I</p>||||||||
\* Watchers don’t have a corporeal body.

A Watcher’s Willpower, Logic, Intuition and Charisma are equal to its Force divided by 2 (round up).



**<a name="_toc218024807"></a>MENTOR SPIRITS**\

==============================================
In the search for magical enlightenment, affiliation or purpose, many Awakened individuals are drawn toward certain animals, mythological figures or concepts. This may be an idol they grew up with, a tribal totem or something they look up to achieve in their life. It could also relate to their religious or magical beliefs. So strong are the feelings for this person or idea that once the individual Awakens, the idea takes a life of its own. It becomes what is known as a mentor spirit.

This mentor spirit is much like other spirits in that it has its own personality, but it’s not a spirit in the summon-and-banish sense of the term. It can be seen and heard by those it chooses and even physically interact with its followers. Your mentor spirit can have significant influence over you, giving you benefits when you remain true or punishing you if you go astray (sometimes with temporary reductions to your Magic rating).

There is no real understanding of the nature of mentor spirits but their goal is clear. They want to keep Awakened individuals on the path that helped introduce the mentor spirit to the Earth in the first place. Any Awakened character can connect with a mentor spirit by taking the Mentor Spirit quality.
### **Mentor Spirit Archetypes**
Each of the mentor spirits listed here represents an archetype. These archetypes are idealised as totem animals, deities and forces of nature by different cultures and traditions. The archetypes listed below serve merely as examples of different archetypes and are not meant to apply to all cultures – a totem animal considered a healer in one culture may be considered a deceiver in another.

Each archetype offers three advantages: one general bonus, one bonus that applied only to magicians and one that applies only to adepts. Each also has a disadvantage. Advantages and disadvantages apply at all times.
#### **Bear**
This mentor symbolises strength and protection. He is a healer and cannot turn down those in need without good reason and he defends those under his care. Bear is more than a gentle healer; he is a ferocious protector, disregarding his own safety in combat if wounded or if someone he is protecting is injured.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to resist damage (not including Drain)

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus for Health spells, preparations and rituals

**Adept**: 1 free level of Rapid Healing

**Disadvantages**

You might go berserk when you take Physical damage in combat or if someone under your care is badly injured. Make a Simple Charisma + Willpower Test (wound modifiers apply). You go berserk for 3 turns minus 1 turn per hit, so 3 or more hits avert the berserk rage entirely. If you’re already going berserk, increase the duration. When you’re berserk, you go after your attacker(s) without regard for your own safety. If you incapacitate the target(s) before the time is up, the berserk fury dissipates.
#### **Cat**
Cat is honoured in cultures around the world. Cat is often seen as the guardian of mystical secrets, including those involving the afterlife. She certainly knows many secrets but rarely decides to share them and never with anyone who is not worthy. She is stealthy, sly and arrogant. Cat toys with her prey – threatening, taunting and confusing her targets – rather than going directly for the kill.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to either Acrobatics or Stealth Tests (choose one)

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus for Illusion spells, preparations and rituals

**Adept**: 2 free levels of Light Body

**Disadvantages**

Cat magicians toy with their prey. Unless you succeed in a Charisma + Willpower (3) Test at the start of combat, you cannot make an attack that incapacitates your target. If you take any Physical damage, all this playing around stops.
#### **Dog**
Dog is a loyal friend. He fights ferociously to defend his home and those under his protection. Dog protects people from harmful magic and dangerous spirits. Dog is loyal, generous and helpful to those who show him kindness. He is single-minded, often to the point of stubbornness.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to Tracking Tests

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus to Detection spells, preparations and rituals

**Adept**: 2 free levels of Improved Sense

**Disadvantages**

A Dog magician is stubbornly loyal. You can never leave someone behind, betray your comrades or let another sacrifice themselves in your place without making a successful Charisma + Willpower (3) Test.
#### **Dragonslayer**
This most heroic of mentor spirits is also the most fun loving. Though he fights to protect his own against all dangers, he loves a good party even more. He is a big brother who takes a friendly interest in everything his family does. Though sometimes naïve, he makes a staunch friend and a deadly enemy. The dragons he slays have changed with the times: current beasts include crime, pollution, corruption and, of course, actual dragons. Dragonslayer fights hard and plays hard. Once he has given his oath, he never breaks it. A Dragonslayer magician behaves with honour and respect and demands the same from those around him.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to one social skill of choice

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus to Combat spells, preparations and rituals

**Adept**: 1 free level of Enhanced Accuracy (skill) and 1 free level of Danger Sense

**Disadvantages**

If you break a promise, whether by choice or accident, you take a -1 dice pool modifier to all actions until you make good on your promise or atone.
#### **Fitness Guru**
Often devoted to self-improvement, those who follow the mentor spirit of fitness treat their bodies as their greatest instrument. Proud not just of their appearance, but of the power and finesse of their motion and actions. A Fitness magician offers respect to those they deem deserve it but at least politeness to those who don’t. However, they demand that others show them respect.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to Acrobatics Tests

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus to Health spells, preparations and rituals

**Adept**: 2 free levels of Light Body

**Disadvantages**

Followers of this mentor spirit demand respect, especially to those they give it to. Once disrespected, they must succeed in a Charisma + Willpower (3) Test, or they will demand satisfaction against the slight. 
#### **Eagle**
Eagle is the highest-flying bird in the sky, considered the most noble by many cultures. He is proud and solitary and sees everything happening in the world below. Eagles are noble defenders of the purity of nature. They are intolerant of those who do not share their views and have a strong distrust of technology and its tools. Those who damage nature are Eagle’s enemies and Eagle will brave great danger to defeat polluters and other evildoers.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to Perception Tests

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus for summoning spirits of air

**Adept**: 1 free level of Combat Sense

**Disadvantages**

You get the Allergy – Mild Pollutants quality with no bonus Karma for this negative quality.
#### **Oak**
Followers of Oak are stalwart and silent. They listen to the world around them and calculate their next action. A follower may be slow to act, but when they make their move, they do it with conviction. He protects others, shielding small plants and moss from the elements. Strong shields, buildings and ships are made from Oak. Followers protect anyone they have agreed to defend steadfastly, even unto death.

**Advantages**

**All**: +1 dice pool bonus to Damage Resistance Tests

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus for summoning spirits of earth or plant spirits (choose 1 when selecting this mentor spirit)

**Adept**: 2 free levels of Stillness for free.

**Disadvantages**

Must have a natural (meaning unaugmented) Body and Strength of 4 or greater to select this mentor spirit.
#### **Rat**
Rat is found wherever humans and the things they discard are, for what other bounty can sustain him? Rat is a scavenger, a stealthy thief who takes what he needs to survive. He dislikes working out in the open, preferring to stick to the shadows. Rat avoids fights whenever he can – when he must fight, he fights to kill quickly and move on.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to Stealth Tests

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus to Alchemy Tests when harvesting reagents and you may use reagents from other traditions

**Adept**: 2 free levels of Natural Immunity

**Disadvantages**

You must make a Charisma + Willpower (3) Test to not immediately flee or seek cover whenever caught in a combat situation. If there is nowhere to flee, they are forced to fight.
#### **Raven**
Raven is a harbinger of trouble in cultures worldwide. He is a trickster and a transformer, dark and devious. Raven thrives off the bounty of carnage and chaos but does not cause them – he merely knows an opportunity when he sees one. Raven loves to eat and rarely refuses an offer of food.

Raven is cousin to Coyote, who shares trickster inclinations with Raven but lacks his darkness and propensity for carnage.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to Con Tests

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus to Manipulation spells, preparations and rituals

**Adept**: Free Traceless Walk and 1 level of Voice Control

**Disadvantages**

You must make a Charisma + Willpower (3) Test to avoid exploiting someone else’s misfortune to your own advantage or to pull a clever trick or prank even if it’s to the disadvantage of your friends.
#### **Spider**
Spider is one of the more feared and despised totems in the Sixth World. The threat posed by insect spirits is never far from the world’s consciousness and most metahumans still group spiders together with insects (although they are arachnids, scientifically speaking). But the fear of spiders goes deeper than that. Metahumanity has an almost biological fear of spiders, and for good evolutionary reasons, but that isn’t all Spider is. As many cultures know, Spider is not just one thing.

Also known as Anansi, Iktomi or Grandfather Spider, this totem has adapted quite well to the Sixth World. In regions across the globe, Spider presents as a trickster, schemer and hunter. Followers of Spider embody all of these traits and see Spider not as a boogeyman, but as a wise and powerful patron.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to Stealth Tests

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus to Manipulation spells, preparations and rituals

**Adept**: 2 free levels of Spirit Claw (although, in this case it manifests as a fang).

**Disadvantages**

Spider followers, like their mentor, become anxious when events happen beyond their control. As such, they go to great lengths to limit the randomness of their encounters. When not following a plan or a plan doesn’t go according to plan, followers of Spider must pass a Charisma + Willpower (4) Test or suffer -2 to all rolls until a new plan is established.
#### **Wise Warrior**
The Wise Warrior is skilled in the art of war, for battle is an art to them, an exercise in the powers of the mind as well as the body. They study the tactics of their foes and overcome them through a combination of superior strategy and battle prowess. The Wise Warrior does not act out of savagery or battle-lust, but from a position of knowledge and wisdom. Wise Warriors must follow the warrior’s code of honour and conduct themselves properly or risk the loss of favour.

**Advantages**

**All**: +2 dice pool bonus to Leadership Tests

**Magician**: +2 dice pool bonus to Combat spells, preparations and rituals

**Adept**: 1 free level of Improved Ability on a Combat Skill

**Disadvantages**

If you act dishonourably or without courtesy, whether by choice or by accident, you take a -1 dice pool penalty to all actions until you atone for your behaviour.


**<a name="_toc218024808"></a>FOCI**\

====================================
Foci are more than mundane items with a dusting of mana to give them potency. They are astral constructs embedded within physical objects. When active, the design of the astral construct enhances mana energy so that the magician it is bonded to can draw upon it for a specific magical task. The physical form of a focus varies – amulets, belts, wands, walking sticks, cups, daggers, hip flasks, pens and so on and so forth – although most of the time a focus reflects the tradition of its maker. Foci have a Force Rating that measures their power.

You can’t use a focus unless you’ve bonded it to yourself (and you can’t bond foci unless you’re Awakened). Bonding a focus takes an hour per Force of the Focus, spent contemplating the object and synchronising its astral signature to yours. A focus can only be bound to one person at a time – the bonding process breaks the bond with the focus’s previous owner (if it had one).

` `Each focus has a specific power and must be active for you to use it. Activating a focus is a Simple Action. For a focus to remain active, it must be in the possession of the magician (worn, carried, hand-held, in a pocket or pouch, etc). Likewise, if you lose consciousness your foci deactivate. If you lose possession of a focus, it automatically deactivates and you lose all its benefits until you recover it and activate it again. You can deactivate a focus at any time with a Bonus Action.

All foci have auras that are visible from astral space and carry your astral signature. While activated, a focus also has an astral form. If you use astral projection, you also carry the astral form of any active foci you have. If you deactivate a focus while you’re projecting, its astral form disappears and you’ll need to go back to your body to reactivate it.

You can’t bond more foci that your Magic attribute and the maximum Force of all your bonded foci can’t exceed your Magic x5. Regardless of the number of bonded foci you have, only one focus may add its Force to a dice pool for any given test.

|**Focus Item**|**Bonding Cost (Karma)**|
| :- | :- |
|**Enchanting Focus**|Force x3|
|**Metamagic Focus**|Force x3|
|**Power Focus**|Force x6|
|**Qi Focus**|Force x2|
|**Spell Focus**|Force x2|
|**Spirit Focus**|Force x2|
|**Weapon Focus**|Force x3|
### **Focus Types**
There are several categories of foci: Enchanting, Power, Qi, Spirit, Sorcery and Weapon.
#### **Enchanting Foci**
**Alchemical**: An alchemical focus adds its Force in dice to any Alchemical Tests.

**Artificing**: An artificing focus adds its Force in dice to any Artificing Tests.

**Disenchanting**: When a disenchanting focus is in contact with another artifact, the magician can add dice equal to its Force to the Disenchanting Test.
#### **Power Foci**
Power foci temporarily increase your dice pools when using Sorcery, Conjuring or Enchanting.

**Conjuring**: A conjuring focus adds dice equal to its Force to Banishing, Binding and Summoning Tests.

**Enchanting**: An enchanting focus adds dice equal to its Force to Alchemy, Artificing and Disenchanting Tests.

**Sorcery**: A sorcery focus adds dice equal to its Force to Counterspelling, Ritual Magic and Spellcasting Tests.
#### **Qi Foci**
Qi foci only work for adepts. They channel mana into your adept powers. A qi focus can be an object, like other foci, but can also be worked into a body modification, like tattoos, ritual scarring and piercings. Each focus is specific to a single adept power at a specific level. While the focus is active, you get the power contained in it, or if you already have the power, the focus’s levels are added to your own (if it’s a power with levels).
#### **Spirit Foci**
Spirit foci empower a magician’s conjuring skills. Each spirit focus must be attuned to a specific type of spirit.

**Summoning**: A summoning focus adds dice equal to its Force to summoning attempts as long as the targeted spirit is in the same category as the focus.

**Banishing**: The banishing focus adds its Force to the limit of a magician’s Banishing Test as long as the target spirit is in the same category as the focus.

**Binding**: A binding focus helps a magician tie a spirit to them. The focus adds its Force in dice to the magician’s Binding Test as long as the spirit is in the same category as the focus.
#### **Sorcery Foci**
Sorcery foci empower a magician’s sorcery skills. Each sorcery focus must be attuned to a specific category of magic. 

**Counterspelling**: A counterspelling focus adds dice equal to its Force to counterspelling attempts as long as the category of magic is the same category as the focus.

**Ritual Magic**: A ritual magic focus adds dice equal to its Force to Ritual Magic Tests as long as the category of magic is the same category as the focus.

**Spellcasting**: A spellcasting focus adds dice equal to its Force to Spellcasting Tests as long as the category of magic is the same category as the focus.
#### **Weapon Foci**
A weapon focus always has, unsurprisingly, the form of a melee weapon. It adds magical power to the melee attacks you make with it. When used in physical combat, it gives you its Force as a dice pool bonus on your melee Attack Test. You still rely on your Physical Attributes and skills in combat; the weapon focus merely makes you more effective.

A weapon focus is effective against astral forms too, whether you’re using astral perception or projection. It adds its Force to your Astral Combat Tests when you’re using it and you can take it along while astrally projecting. The damage of the weapon in astral combat is the same as it is in the physical world, except that you can decide between Stun or Physical damage.


**<a name="_toc218024809"></a>THE MATRIX**\

==========================================
### **What is the Matrix?**
We use it every day to read out email, pay our bills, talk to our friends and loved ones. It monitors our money, handles our utilities and manages the traffic on our streets. Billons of people use it constantly, from the hungry family in Redmond to the CEO in Neo-Tokyo and everyone in between. It is the Matrix, the digital world within a world made of fibre-optic cables, networks and more data and computing power than has ever existed in the history of the planet. A record that exists today so it can be broken tomorrow.
### **Wireless World**
The paradox of the Matrix is this: to be an ace hacker, you need to understand it – but no one really understands it. Like so many things, though, the real key is to know more and be better than the next guy. So, let’s get you started with a quick overview of the Matrix experience.
### **The Local Mesh**
This is the part of the Matrix that relies on device-to-device connections and is called the **local mesh** or sometimes the **lower grid**. The extreme density of devices in a 2075 city, combined with the ability to seamlessly pass traffic from device to device, can get your signal where it needs to go. The local mesh has a strictly limited range: too many hops, too much distance or too much interference and the signal degrades and becomes useless. Fortunately, for a legitimate user, their network traffic only needs to reach an **uplink node**, so this is rarely an issue. Any two or more Matrix devices within range of each other can form a local mesh, even if they cannot route a signal out to the wider Matrix. They will still be able to communicate with themselves as normal.
### **Uplink Nodes**
When you want to communicate with a device that’s outside local mesh range, first you need an **uplink node**. These are scattered around major metropolitan areas. Your device sends traffic along the local mesh until it reaches the nearest or most convenient uplink node. Uplinks serve as the onramps to the rest of the Matrix; they bridge your traffic over to the backbone. Uplink nodes are sometimes called beanstalks by deckers, because they lead to the clouds.
### **The Backbone**
The **backbone** or the **upper grid**, is the planet-sized interconnected network of fibre cables, satellites, microwave and visible-laser point-to-point communications and other bleeding-edge-tech ways of getting 1s and 0s from A to B. Once your traffic is on the backbone, distance is no object and bandwidth is functionally infinite. Security on uplink nodes is fierce and traffic on the backbone is routinely subjected to deep packet inspection.
### **Commlinks**
Commlinks are the most visible part of the Matrix – the device most commonly associated with it in people’s minds. They are analogous to modern-day smartphones and often take the form of a pocket-sized slab covered in a touchscreen (although they can be much smaller if the user forgoes the screen).

Most people using a commlink do so via a **direct neural interface** (DNI) and **augmented reality** (AR).

DNI gives the user a limited amount of mental control directly over the device, without needing to look at the device or push any buttons. DNI is not telepathy. The user can issue simple on/off, less/more, scroll up/down type commands but not much that is more complicated than that. They can also dictate text but only at the speed that is a few times faster than talking. DNI is tiring to use for long period, as it requires close concentration of a particular kind for the machine to detect the commands. It’s like maintaining a fully spoken inner monologue. Few people can keep that up all day long.

AR means the commlink’s output – mostly visual and audio, some tactile – is projected directly into the user’s consciousness. They see pop-up windows floating in their vision, hear sounds overlaid with the real world, feel the weight and texture of virtual “objects” they touch. Each distinct element of an augmented reality user interface is called an **augmented reality object** (ARO), pronounced “arrow”. AROs can come from your commlink itself, like a messaging window for a control palette. They can be broadcast from nearby devices, like a restaurant displaying a holographic menu outside its door or a friend showing you a selfie they took. Or they can be sent to you from items you are carrying, such as a smartgun displaying remaining ammunition count in a discreet window in the corner of your eye. Because pure DNI control requires mental effort, less hardcore users sometimes fall back to either physical controls or (more often) AROs displaying control surfaces. These are less tiring and can be more precise when very delicate control is needed. User interface AROs accessed via DNI have a tactile component, so the user feels like they are interacting with real physical objects that have weight, texture and temperature.
### **PANs**
Most individuals have multiple electronic devices on them at once and having icons for each one show up would provide too much visual clutter in the Matrix. Often, what shows up instead is an icon representing an individual’s personal area network. This icon often looks similar to the physical device that serves as master for the network, such as a commlink or cyberdeck, but individuals will sometimes choose a design or logo that means something to them (such as sports team logos, Concrete Dreams album covers or corporate designs). Some devices are not merged into the single **PAN** icon; if an individual is carrying a wireless-enabled gun – or another wireless device that might kill you – if may show up separately so that it can be identified rapidly. Unless, of course, the user has gone to the trouble to hide that icon, but that’ll be covered later.

Devices can be slaved to a commlink or cyberdeck. The group consisting of slaved devices plus the master commlink or cyberdeck is called a personal area network, or PAN.


**<a name="_toc218024810"></a>WIRELESS DEVICES**\

================================================
Wireless devices are rated for their power and efficiency based on a number of factors and well as having information about their current use status. Below are the ratings and statuses that a wireless device may have.

**Device Rating**: The device rating is a generic rating for standard devices that don’t have more detailed ratings listed.

**Response**: Response is the processing power and speed of the device’s hardware. Response is used for Matrix Initiative. Response is negatively affected when you run too many programs.

**Signal**: Signal represents the broadcasting power of the device’s hardware. The higher the Signal, the farther the device can transmit and the more signal-noise it can cut through.

**Firewall**: Firewall is the device’s built-in security software. It protects against unauthorised access and fends off hostile access attempts and exploits. Firewall is also used to defend against Matrix attacks in cybercombat.

**System**: System measures the power of the device’s operating system (OS) software.
